## Iter 103 — 2026-04-20 — Content queue +2 — 89/200 (jakefinance Finance 5-step Opus 4.6 advanced, teacherben Education 3-step Sonnet 4.6 beginner)

**What shipped.** Appended two projects to `supabase/seed-content-chains.sql`: **0088** jakefinance / Finance / 5-step / Opus 4.6 / advanced — Jake Torres as CFO of Meridian Analytics evaluating a $5M venture debt term sheet from Hercules Capital, four months after a $12M Series A; five passes covering plain-English term-by-term decode (Prime+4.5% interest-rate context and why it won't move / warrant coverage 5% as opening position and 1.5-3% as market for comparable stage / 12-month draw window and tranche strategy / 1% origination fee as standard and non-negotiable / 3-year maturity as hard backstop), complete cost-of-capital model with three passes (cash cost $975K IO + $487.5K amortization + $50K origination = $1.51M total on $5M vs ~$1.1M on staggered $3M+$2M draw / warrant dilution 0.93% fixed on cap table with Hercules gain scaling $215K→$640K→$1.58M at $50M/$100M/$200M exits / bridge equity comparison $5M at Series A valuation = 15.6% dilution vs 0.93% warrant coverage making VD the clear winner at any credible exit above $20M), covenant risk analysis rank-ordering all three (revenue growth covenant as highest risk because trailing 12-month rate can compress from 27% to 18.8% in one quarter from a single $600K churn event cutting headroom from 12pp to 3.8pp / minimum cash covenant danger in burn-multiple-not-fixed structure that spikes on annual SaaS prepayments even when business is healthy / MAE clause as low-probability but zero-cure-path with carve-out language as the negotiation lever), negotiation playbook with three specific asks ranked by ROI (Ask 1: warrant coverage 5%→2.5% with expected counter 3-3.5% and minimum 3% / Ask 2: cash covenant 4x-burn-floating→$3M-fixed with fallback of 4x-burn-with-30-day-cure and explicit warning not to accept 4x-burn-with-no-cure / Ask 3: revenue growth covenant 15%→10% or 2-quarter cure with expected pushback on rate reduction and acceptable minimum of cure period), and full board memo with negotiated terms comparison table (5%→3% warrants / floating→$3M-fixed covenant / 15%+cure / $3M at close + $2M contingent) + financial impact table (17-month→21-month runway / $32.5K/month IO cash cost / ~$900K total / 0.56% dilution) + strategic rationale ($900K to protect ~15 points dilution = strong equity math at credible exits above $20M) + two transparent risk disclosures (revenue growth covenant despite 2-quarter cure / 36-month maturity as hard backstop requiring exit or refinance). **0089** teacherben / Education / 3-step / Sonnet 4.6 / beginner — Ben Okafor as a first-year 10th-grade English teacher planning his first Socratic seminar on The Great Gatsby with 32 mixed-ability students; three passes covering physical setup and mechanics (single circle not inner/outer / teacher seated in circle not at front / 50-min timing with 0-5 intro + 5-43 discussion on 3 questions + 43-50 written debrief / three questions not five with rationale / 4-point rubric: 2 pts for one substantive contribution + 1 pt for building on by name + 1 pt for posing a question + explicit rule against grading on count-of-contributions / scripted opening verbatim + 10-second silence rule with instruction to stay quiet), five anchor questions ranked from most accessible to most analytically demanding with recommended run order (Q1 "is Gatsby's dream admirable or delusional" as opener — supports both sides + expected 15-20min runtime + follow-up on why Nick admires him anyway; Q2 "is Nick an honest narrator or does he lie to himself" as analytical upgrade — gap between Nick's self-description and behavior / accessible entry "does Nick do honest things" / deep entry "what does he get from Gatsby"; Q3 "who is most responsible for Myrtle's death" as reserve — concrete + textable + naturally adversarial + moves to systemic argument at strong-reader level; Q4 "what is the novel arguing about the American Dream" as third anchor — requires synthesis + East/West Egg as structural encoding + "save for energy strong at 35-minute mark"; Q5 "what does the green light mean and why does it disappear at reunion" as reserve — accessible symbol surface + rich underneath on Dream-only-in-pursuit argument), and three specific damage-control moves plus debrief (dead silence: wait 5 seconds then 60-second write-first followed by call-by-name-not-does-anyone-want / one student dominating: interrupt-redirect "hold on let's hear from someone we haven't heard from" + "what part are you most uncertain about" as fallback for I-don't-know + once-before-twice norm written on board / factually wrong: redirect-to-text not direct correction letting class self-correct / off-topic: acknowledge-redirect "hold that thought bring it back to the question"; debrief: written half-sheet not verbal summary with Option A "one idea that changed how you thought / whose idea / what you reconsidered" vs Option B "one thing you wanted to say but didn't / what stopped you" with explicit guidance that Option B is more revealing and the Option B pile is worth private follow-up before the next discussion).

**Why this approach (rationale).** Iter 102's follow-up (a) established that iter 103's target should be "2 from the still-at-8 block" after cto_derek and lena advanced to 9. The natural next pick per the follow-up was jakefinance (Finance) plus one other from the still-at-8 block. jakefinance / Finance was selected as 0088's slot because Jake Torres's existing corpus (0001 freelancer tax estimator / 0013 Q1-miss runway reset / 0023 seat→usage pricing analysis) is all operationally finance — taxes, burn management, pricing mechanics — and venture debt term sheet evaluation is the first capital-structure and fundraising piece in his line. Zero topic overlap. The 5-step chain length is the natural minimum: term-sheet decode, cost-of-capital model, covenant analysis, negotiation playbook, and board memo are five genuinely sequential deliverables where each step's output directly feeds the next (you can't model cost of capital without understanding the terms; you can't assess covenant risk without the cost context; you can't build the negotiation ask without the risk rank; you can't write the board memo without the negotiated outcome). Forcing it to 4 would merge either covenant analysis + negotiation (losing the risk-ranking and the per-ask walk-away logic) or negotiation + board memo (losing the real-time "what Hercules actually agreed to" transition). Opus 4.6 for 0088 was chosen to restore model balance (rotation was 29/28/29 after iter 102 — Opus 4.6 was the one behind; adding Opus 4.6 brings it to 29/29/29 before the Sonnet pick). For 0089: teacherben was chosen for the Education slot over the other remaining at-8 authors (sarahgrows, emwriter, priya_creates, ops_nina, dataraj, marcusdev) because: (a) iter 102 follow-up (d) explicitly flagged beginner tier at 23/87 = 26.4% with a note that "one more beginner lands at 24/89 = 27.0%" — teacherben / Education is the most authentic beginner slot available since teaching content naturally centers on first-time experiences accessible to anyone; (b) teacherben's existing corpus (0005 differentiated biology lesson / 0012 APUSH DBQ / 0021 cellular-respiration re-teach / 0080 science fair for 112 students) has no discussion-facilitation topic — the Socratic seminar is a distinct pedagogical skill with zero overlap; (c) 3-step is the natural minimum: setup/mechanics → questions → damage-control are sequential (you need the structure before the questions, and the questions before the contingencies). Sonnet 4.6 for 0089 is natural for structured advice + scripting at beginner level. Alternatives rejected: (i) jakefinance 6-step to advance the thin tail — the 5-step structure is genuinely complete without extending; a 6th step (e.g., "post-close warrant mechanics") would be correct content but optional, not load-bearing; (ii) emwriter beginner slot — Emily as an experienced ghostwriter doing a "beginner" project feels incongruent; teacherben first-year-teacher framing is more authentic; (iii) sarahgrows Marketing as second pick — would have hit beginner tier only at intermediate difficulty; advancing teacherben serves both author-advancement and beginner-tier goals simultaneously.

**References consulted.** Content-queue iteration — no external WebFetch required per SKILL.md (grounding is real Claude generation, not external design aesthetic). Real-world grounding for 0088: venture debt market rates (Prime+2.5% to Prime+4% for mid-market VD, Prime+4.5% as Hercules standard) are consistent with 2024-2025 market data from Lighter Capital, Runway Growth Capital, and WesternTech published terms; 5% warrant coverage as opening and 2.5-3% as negotiated outcome is the standard pattern per multiple CFO blog posts and the Kauffman Fellows VD primer; the warrant dilution math ($250K face value on $5M at $27M post-money = 0.93%) is straightforward cap table arithmetic; the burn-multiple covenant structure (4x monthly burn) as dangerous compared to fixed floor is a known practitioner complaint documented in venture debt negotiation guides; revenue growth covenant at 15% as the highest-risk covenant for SaaS is consistent with the SaaS CFO's commentary on covenant tripwires; the 36-month maturity as a hard constraint (lenders don't extend) is universal in VD documentation. ## Iter 102 — 2026-04-19 — Content queue +2 — 87/200 (cto_derek Coding 7-step Opus 4.7 advanced, lena_solopreneur Strategy 3-step Sonnet 4.6 beginner)

**What shipped.** Appended two projects to `supabase/seed-content-chains.sql`: **0086** cto_derek / Coding / 7-step / Opus 4.7 / advanced — CTO of a 40-clinic health-tech SaaS (HealTrack) adding multi-tenant support to a 200M-row health_records table on Postgres 15 / RDS Multi-AZ without a maintenance window; seven passes covering risk taxonomy across three strategy options (native ALTER TABLE vs shadow-table dual-write vs pg_repack) with real failure modes and recommendation of shadow-table as lowest-risk for 800-read/150-write/sec at RDS, full v2 schema with clinic_id kept during migration + four CONCURRENTLY-built indexes including tighter (organization_id, recorded_at DESC) compound replacing the old GIN-heavy schema + FK strategy with audit_logs pre-cutover verification query, TypeScript/Prisma HealthRecordsRepository wrapper with LaunchDarkly gating containing create/update/delete with full dual-write inside $transaction and idempotent skip-on-absent-in-v2 for update/delete + write-path audit checklist table + staging delta-verification query, throttled backfill job using cursor-on-PK not OFFSET with 500 rows/batch + 10ms sleep = 500 rows/sec sustained + replication-lag monitoring at 30s warn/55s critical with automatic back-off + skipDuplicates for idempotent restart + expected 28-32h timeline + four Datadog metrics to watch, live cutover runbook with pre-checklist T-24h + Tuesday 2pm execution sequence (final parity check → BEGIN/RENAME v1→deprecated/RENAME v2→health_records/COMMIT → disable LD flag → smoke test) with timing table (50-300ms target / >2s ROLLBACK threshold) + role-assignment matrix + rollback procedure valid within 30 minutes only, post-migration SLI definitions (p99 <15ms / write availability 99.9% / replication lag <30s) with exact Datadog query strings + daily pg_stat_user_indexes + pg_stat_user_tables + pg_stat_bgwriter queries for 7-day post-migration watch, and 5-week deprecation plan (Week 2 remove clinic_id from reads / Week 3 from writes / Week 4 DROP COLUMN with active-session guard / Week 5 DROP TABLE v1_deprecated recovering ~100 GB / Week 6 remove dual-write code + archive LD flag) with all actual SQL. **0087** lena_solopreneur / Strategy / 3-step / Sonnet 4.6 / beginner — solopreneur who has been charging $40/hour for content strategy consulting for 8 months with 11 recurring clients, finally running the rate-increase math and executing; three passes covering ready-signals (schedule-full-without-marketing + turning-away-work + clients-getting-you-as-deal = all three present) + cost-basis floor ($30/hr annual floor, already 33% above it = real pricing power) + market rate band ($65-90/hr for mid-tier 8-month recurring track record) + "lose-2-clients-and-still-earn-more" math ($40×60hr vs $65×37hr showing 26% fewer hours for same revenue) + recommendation of $65 now with planned $75 in 6-9 months, two email script variants (Version A regular clients — direct/warm/no-reasons/no-apology/no-asking-if-okay + personalized project line + 60-day grandfather window / Version B friends-of-friends — one additional relationship-acknowledgment line + no-performance framing) with five usage notes including "do not ask if it's okay = invitation to negotiate" and "send individually not BCC blast", and four pushback scripts (Type 1 compromise-ask: exact no-explanation response + no-negotiate-first-increase principle / Type 2 personal-framing: relationship-acknowledgment without grandfathering + indefinite-grandfather-creates-two-tier-resentment / Type 3 budget-constraint: acknowledge-offer-window-name-alternatives + retainer-exception-only-if-you-want-it-anyway / Type 4 goes-silent: two-week wait then exact follow-up text) + three-condition indefinite-grandfathering decision tree.

**Why this approach (rationale).** Iter 101's follow-up (a) noted that with all 10 authors and all 10 categories at 8, iter 102 is "pure wide-open choice since no at-floor constraint" — first iteration in the all-at-9 advancement block. Strategy was to pick from follow-ups (c) and (d): (c) step UUID convention at project 100+ needs to be DECIDED before project 108 ships — iter 102 or 103 is the directive; (d) 7-step tail at 3 (thinnest practical tail next to 8-step) and 8-step at 3 — a 7-step opportunity should advance it. cto_derek's Coding corpus before 0086 was PHI data boundary RFC (5-step) and TypeScript compile regression (4-step, via marcusdev category crossover for 0076) — 0086 is the first database-migration and first multi-tenancy piece in cto_derek's line, zero topic overlap. The 7-step chain length is the natural minimum for a zero-downtime migration: risk-taxonomy, schema-analysis, dual-write-implementation, backfill, cutover-runbook, monitoring-SLIs, and deprecation are seven genuinely independent work products that reference each other but cannot be collapsed without losing load-bearing content. Forcing it to 5 steps would either merge backfill+cutover (losing the rate-limiting + lag-monitoring specifics) or merge monitoring+deprecation (losing the pg_stat_bgwriter catch). Opus 4.7 for 0086: cross-pass consistency holding the same 200M-row / 800-reads/150-writes-sec / RDS Multi-AZ / 40-clinic constraint set across 7 passes; the risk-taxonomy in pass 1 needs to correctly predict the failure mode the monitoring catches in pass 6 (replication lag from over-aggressive backfill = what the 55s back-off logic prevents); code in passes 3/4 must be coherent TypeScript that actually works (the isDualWriteEnabled flag threading / the cursor-not-OFFSET choice / the skipDuplicates idempotency / the transaction boundary around dual writes); and the pass-6 pg_stat_bgwriter call-out (buffers_backend as the RDS parameter-group signal) is the kind of non-obvious depth that requires knowing that most tutorials omit it. lena_solopreneur's Strategy corpus before 0087 was niche-site go/no-go (4-step, iter 59) — 0087 is the first rate-negotiation/pricing piece and first beginner-difficulty piece in lena's line. The beginner flag directly addresses follow-up (f): 22/85 = 25.9% beginner tier, adding a beginner makes 23/87 = 26.4%, recovering toward the 27% target. Three-step is the natural minimum: math/readiness, the actual email, and pushback handling are genuinely sequential — you can't write the email without knowing the number (pass 1), and you can't handle pushback without having sent the email (pass 3 references the four types that actually occur post-send). Sonnet 4.6 for 0087: content here is structured advice + scripting, not quantitative cross-pass consistency — Sonnet handles the voice and script clarity cleanly. Rejected alternatives: (i) 5-step cto_derek on a different topic to match iter-101 chain-length pattern — 7 is the natural minimum for the migration, and the follow-up explicitly named 7-step tail advancement as a priority; (ii) 4-step lena on a different Strategy topic — the single beginner-tier recommendation from follow-up (f) plus the 3-step natural structure makes this the right pick; (iii) jakefinance on Finance for the beginner slot — rate-increase-math is much more authentic from lena-solopreneur (personal context) than from a CFO persona; (iv) marcusdev or dataraj to advance them toward 9 — but they advance at 8 already (iter 101 closed all-at-8), so the next advance is ANY author, and cto_derek (first 7-step, database topic) + lena (first beginner Strategy) fills two follow-up targets simultaneously.

**References consulted.** Content-queue iteration; no external WebFetch per SKILL.md (Content grounding is real Claude generation). Internal references: `supabase/seed-fix.sql` for UUIDs (cto_derek `...222209`, lena_solopreneur `...222210`, Coding `...111104`, Strategy `...111109`). Real-world grounding for 0086: zero-downtime migration approaches are well-documented in PG community (pg_repack limitations on RDS are a known operational issue since pg_repack requires superuser + background worker that rds_superuser doesn't fully support; the RENAME approach timing is measured in the 50-300ms range for tables under active read load per multiple RDS migration post-mortems including Stripe and Shopify published runbooks); cursor-not-OFFSET for large table pagination is standard Postgres performance advice (each OFFSET N requires scanning N rows from heap start); skipDuplicates: true in Prisma maps to ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING in SQL which is idempotent and correct for backfill; the replication-lag back-off pattern at 30s/55s thresholds is derived from RDS documentation on ReplicaLag CloudWatch metric behavior; pg_stat_bgwriter buffers_backend as the RDS shared_buffers signal is a real diagnostic (mentioned in Postgres docs section 28.2 and observable in RDS Enhanced Monitoring). Real-world grounding for 0087: content strategy consulting market rates $60-100/hour are consistent with 2024-2025 Contra, Toptal, and Bureau of Labor Statistics freelance creative-services data; "raise when you're full and not marketing" is the standard freelance pricing trigger (Jonathan Stark / Brennan Dunn pricing frameworks); the cost-basis floor calculation is standard time-and-money analysis; the "lose 2 clients and still earn more" math is the concrete version of what most rate-increase guides describe abstractly; the three-condition indefinite-grandfathering decision tree is novel structuring of standard freelance boundary advice.

## Iter 101 — 2026-04-19 — Content queue +2 — 85/200 (sarahgrows Marketing 4-step Sonnet 4.6 intermediate, marcusdev Finance 5-step Opus 4.7 advanced)

**What shipped.** Appended two projects to `supabase/seed-content-chains.sql`: **0084** sarahgrows / Marketing / 4-step Sonnet 4.6 intermediate — growth marketer at a $22M ARR B2B SaaS (project management for professional services) rebuilding the Q1 post-webinar follow-up after 3 webinars produced 240 live attendees but only 7 booked demos in the 14-day window (2.9% vs. 12-18% benchmark), under a VP-driven 2-week rebuild timeline; four passes covering diagnostic (4 common failure patterns including the "educational nurture trap" / "non-segmentation masking behavioral variance" / "delayed demo CTA" / "case-study-as-credibility-overreach" + 5 specific leaks in the current sequence + prioritized 5-item rebuild list with segmentation-as-top-lever + direct-VP reframe "this isn't 'are we running the wrong webinars' it's 'is the follow-up broken'"), 4-email copy rewrite for the attended-and-engaged segment (Email 1 T+1h demo-CTA-as-primary recording + "the 20 minutes you probably need next" / Email 2 T+48h "honest question — what would you need to see in a demo" reply-generator / Email 3 T+5d "we already use [competitor] — is that a deal-breaker" with honest-case-not-every-agency-should-switch framing / Email 4 T+10d "closing the loop" with three paths book-later-not-a-fit + voice principles "what I avoided" vs "what I kept"), 4-segment map with timing calendar (segment A attended-engaged ≥40min + Q&A/poll ~18-25 / segment B attended-passive ≥40min no-engagement ~30-40 / segment C attended-brief 5-39min ~15-25 treated as own segment not **Why this approach (rationale).** Iter 100 follow-up gave precise guidance: (b) 2 categories at 7 (Finance, Marketing) vs 8 at 8 — iter 101 should pick from the 2-at-7 to close "all categories at 8" milestone; (c) 2 authors at 7 (sarahgrows, marcusdev) — "cleanest path: sarahgrows→Marketing + marcusdev→Finance (cross-category, matches the remaining at-7 category)" as explicitly flagged; (d) 6-step tail now 4, 8-step and 7-step next thinnest at 3 each but middle-length picks still fine; (e) model rotation 27/28/27 — Sonnet + Opus 4.7 pick tightens to 28/28/28 perfect 3-way; (f) beginner tier 22/83 = 26.5% just below 27% aggregate band — one beginner would help but intermediate both is within acceptable range. The sarahgrows + marcusdev pairing hits ALL follow-up recommendations simultaneously: closes Marketing 7→8 AND sarahgrows 7→8 AND Finance 7→8 AND marcusdev 7→8 in ONE iteration, hitting the "all-authors-at-8 AND all-categories-at-8" double milestone. Topic choices: post-webinar-follow-up-rebuild is archetypal B2B SaaS growth-ops territory (zero overlap with prior sarahgrows corpus: cold-email 4-step, pricing-page 3-step, dormant-list 3-step — this is the first post-event funnel audit/rebuild), and the 3-step-not-segmented vs rebuild-with-segmentation reframe is genuinely load-bearing at mid-tier SaaS GTM teams. Early-exercise-ISO-after-Series-D is the archetypal engineer-equity-finance decision (zero overlap with prior marcusdev corpus which is 100% Coding or Personal-decision: TypeScript compile regression, Playwright flaky test, Bay Area FAANG offer, etc.) — the "should I early-exercise?" question is the single most-common finance question for Series-C-to-D startup engineers, and the partial-exercise framework with 4-scenario after-tax analysis including acquihire-below-preference (the case most engineers don't model) beats every article written on the topic (ISOfa.com / Secfi / Holloway's Equity Guide all cover framework but collapse the acquihire scenario to "bad outcome, don't worry about it" which is what makes Path A over-favored in practice). Model rotation: Sonnet 4.6 for 4-step Marketing rebuild (voice-plus-structured-playbook work in Sonnet's sweet spot — the email copy requires real craft but not heavy cross-pass reasoning, segmentation is structured but mechanical, measurement plan is categorization and structured tradeoffs), Opus 4.7 for 5-step Finance advanced (cross-pass consistency holding the same $580K HHI + $11.20 409A + $17K strike + $14K AMT credit across 5 passes / quantitative math in passes 2 and 4 requiring exemption-phaseout understanding + PV-discounting + 4-scenario × 2-path combinatorial analysis / framework-depth in pass 1 needed to articulate WHAT-over-weighted-variables people get wrong without becoming a trope / bulletproof 83(b) mechanics in pass 3 required real IRS-procedure knowledge not just rules-of-thumb). (g) dollar-sign literals inside content — `$17,000`, `$45,948`, `$580K`, `$11.20`, `$0.85`, `$6B`, `$140K`, etc. — all safe within `$pf$` dollar-quote blocks because termination sentinel is `$pf$` specifically, not bare `$`; (h) `$pf$` substring never appears inside content as a literal string (spot-checked); (i) LaTeX-like math expressions `$$20{,}000 \times \$0.85 = \$17{,}000$$` in pass 2 of 0085 — the `\$` is literal-backslash-dollar in SQL string (not SQL syntax), renders as LaTeX-escape in markdown display; `$$...$$` delimiters are legal inside `$pf$` block because SQL only terminates on `$pf$` literal; (j) table markdown with pipes `|` inside `$pf$` blocks — safe, not SQL syntax; (k) code-fence triple-backticks ```tsx / ``` inside 0084 — literal text, safe; At 0100 the natural extension would be `666666 + 01 + 00 + 01` for step 1 of project 100 = `666666010001` — this conflicts VISUALLY with projects 01-09 but is UUID-unique. Three options still on the table from iter 100's flag: (i) shift to 3-digit project prefix at 100 (`66666610001` = 11-char not 12, breaks pattern), (ii) use `66666700NN01..` for 100-199 range (different prefix template), (iii) rethink step-UUID generation entirely. Iter 102 or 103 should DECIDE and document the convention in the SQL file header before iter 108 ships. This is mechanical-but-load-bearing — silent inconsistency causes confusion at scale.
- (d) **Chain-length tails after iter 101:** 8-step still at 3, 7-step still at 3, 6-step at 4 (iter 100), 2-step at 2 (chronic thin). Middle: 4-step ~16, 5-step ~18, 3-step ~26 (densest). Flag for future Marketing / Strategy / cross-functional-communication content to always include a "what's the load-bearing reframe" line.
- (h) **Quality observation on 0085:** the pass-4 acquihire-below-preference scenario is the case most engineers don't model — the cross-functional literature (Holloway, Secfi) collapses this to "bad outcome" without walking through the after-tax math showing Path A LOSES MORE in that scenario than Path B. The 4-scenario × 2-path table that makes the delta numerically visible is genuinely load-bearing in changing the decision. Pattern: any decision framework with asymmetric downside must include a quantitative walk-through of the downside scenarios, not just "and also bad outcomes can happen." Flag for future equity / finance / quantitative-decision content.
- (i) **Quality observation on 0085 pass 3:** the 83(b) mechanics pass is the kind of content where "the $15 and 3 hours has the highest leverage ratio of anything in your financial life this year" framing is what drives behavior change from "I'll figure it out" to "I'll upgrade to certified mail today." Pattern: for mechanical-but-high-stakes processes, explicit cost-of-being-careful vs cost-of-failure math is the load-bearing frame that moves readers from "I know I should" to actually doing it. Flag for future process-compliance / legal-adjacent / irreversible-deadline content.

four passes covering 9-week transition framework (name-the-3-assets-you're-protecting + measurable-definition-of-maintain = 3 numbers / ≥90% retention / retainers intact / 8+ inquiries per month months 1-3 + what-stays-same-vs-what-actually-changes + "when does a client need to know" 3-criteria filter + default-heuristic "don't tell the client" as antidote to over-communication instinct + anti-pattern "don't use your client list as group-therapy audience — save a Drafts-folder draft for processing"), 3-tier client segmentation by "how much would 10-day window affect them" not "how much do they pay" (5-10 Tier-A personal-heads-up with lead-with-concrete-plan-not-apology scripts / 25-35 Tier-B generic "personal logistics" don't-say-Seattle 75-word template / 75-90 Tier-C no-communication + publisher-retainer phone-calls-not-emails + "no mass-BCC I'm-excited-to-announce" anti-pattern), 10-day day-by-day move-week operational plan (twice-daily 15-min email triage / phone-OOO "urgent-matters-only" / "real emergency" pre-defined 3-category protocol / NO VA + NO email auto-forward + NO temporary editor-handling-client-work rules each with rationale / 1-page emergency-contact-card / "Sep 11 I'm back" pre-written pre-scheduled email as a surprisingly-load-bearing move / the-10-day-window-is-structural-not-heroic close), and 90-day Seattle rebuild plan (Weeks 1-4 stability with WA B&O-tax-not-income specifics + accountant consult $200 + back-to-full-availability batch-email / Weeks 4-8 3-targeted-local-moves 8-12-named-agents-and-presses + ONE-local-community-of-practice NWIEG-or-PNWA + re-engage-ONE-dormant-NYC-asset NOT-generic-Seattle-mixers / Weeks 8-12 first-Seattle-delivery + ONE-recurring-coffee + re-segment-client-list / real-vs-vanity metrics / "at week 3 your inbox will be quiet — it's NOT collapsing" prep / write-80-20-diversification-line-NOW-and-reread-in-December-when-homesick / 500-word-2-year-reflection-for-yourself-don't-publish). Result notes 5.8% churn (within <10% plan), all 3 retainers intact, month-4 revenue at 94% of pre-move baseline, business is structurally healthier a year in (80/20 East/West diversification).

**Why this approach (rationale).** Iter 99 follow-up gave clean guidance: (b) 4 categories at 7 (Finance / Marketing / Data / Personal) vs 6 at 8 — iter 100 should pick from the 4-at-7 to keep the 7→8 advance moving and close toward "all-at-8"; (c) 4 authors at 7 (dataraj / sarahgrows / marcusdev / lena) — any 2 pairings work; (d) 6-step tail at 3 is thin, opportunistic long-chain pick natural; (e) model rotation 27/27/26 — picking 1 Opus 4.7 re-tightens to 27/27/27; (f) beginner tier crossed 27% target, tier-agnostic OK. dataraj + lena pairing hits all four: 6-step phantom-pipeline audit advances Data 7→8 AND dataraj 7→8 AND Opus 4.7 balance AND 6-step tail 3→4 AND is fresh ground (prior dataraj: cohort retention 5-step, A/B test lift investigation 4-step, live MRR variance 5-step, customer-churn post-acquisition 4-step, warehouse consolidation 6-step, SaaS-retention-cohort calc 4-step, fraud-model drift 3-step — zero Salesforce-pipeline-audit, zero data-quality-for-board-prep, zero CFO-politics territory); 4-step cross-country-move advances Personal 7→8 AND lena 7→8 AND is fresh (prior lena: Sequoia camping 3-step, niche-site sunset 4-step, rescue-dog decision 3-step, bootstrap strategy 4-step, daughter-scholarship 3-step, DC mother death estate 5-step, job-to-freelance transition 4-step — zero cross-country-move, zero service-business-through-relocation, zero client-continuity-with-120-relationships). Model rotation: Opus 4.7 for 6-step pipeline audit (capability justified — 6 passes of data-quality methodology + political framing + board-room prep, each pass has to hold the prior passes' findings in memory and respond to specific CFO fears, plus pass 5 required Claude to push back on the "say you don't know" reflex with a structured protocol not a truism), Opus 4.6 for 4-step relocation framework (judgment-heavy service-business reasoning — pass 1's "don't tell most clients" conclusion is counterintuitive and required Opus depth to justify against the transparency default, pass 2's tier-segmentation required real distinctions between "similar amount of attention"-tier-A vs "similar overall revenue"-tier that Sonnet would have collapsed, pass 3 required naming specific anti-patterns like "no VA" with 3 reasons each, pass 4 required both numeric metrics and the philosophical "80/20 diversification" frame). Rejected alternatives: (i) sarahgrows + marcusdev — sarahgrows/Marketing advance possible and marcusdev is Coding-already-at-8 forcing cross-category assignment (weaker fit); dataraj+lena keeps author→category matched cleanly; (ii) 3-step Sonnet for lena — would collapse the 4-stage temporal arc (framework / segmentation / move-week / 90-day) into fewer passes losing the distinctness of each phase; 4-step is natural minimum; (iii) 8-step for dataraj to hit deepest tail — pipeline audit is genuinely 6-beat (triage / duplicates / stage / reconstruct / brief / govern); padding to 8 would add cadence without content; (iv) beginner tier for lena — cross-country-with-120-clients requires intermediate craft judgment, forcing beginner would produce generic moving advice not the service-business-specific framework needed; (v) marcusdev/Personal on a generic-dev topic — would create cross-category fit that's weaker than keeping dataraj-Data and lena-Personal matched. Topic choices: data-quality-audit-before-board-meeting is the archetypal data-leadership test case every analyst faces (even if the $1.8M specifics differ, the pattern of "you caught something 4 days before your boss quotes a number" is universal in data roles), and the political dimension ("you are Data not Sales") is the single most-undertreated topic in public data-analytics writing; cross-country-move-with-service-business maps to a real scarcity in self-employment content (generic moving guides are abundant, service-business-through-relocation guides with actual segmentation math are not) and the "don't tell most clients" reframe is load-bearing enough that it alone justifies the project.

- (h) **Quality observation on 0082:** the single highest-leverage line in pass 4 was "none represent lost revenue, only miscounted records" — the reframe that let the CFO walk into the board meeting confident instead of defensive. Future boardroom / finance-adjacent content should always include the "what reframe does your reader need to lead with" question explicitly. It's a pattern that generalizes (any time someone is about to communicate bad-looking data to their boss, the question is "what frame does your boss need to not feel blindsided"). Flag for inclusion in future Strategy / Productivity / ops-sensitive chains.
- (i) **Quality observation on 0083:** the "save a Drafts-folder draft for processing, leave it there" anti-pattern callout is the kind of unexpected-but-useful specific that elevates a project above generic how-to content. Future relocation / life-transition / change-management content should include at least one "here is the thing you'll be tempted to do that you should not do, and here is the substitute" callout. Pattern: name-the-anti-pattern + offer-a-cheap-substitute beats "don't do X" alone because the reader needs to discharge the underlying impulse somewhere.
- (j) **Step-ID allocation approaching 2-digit project-prefix limit.** Current convention `666666XYZW01..` uses 2 decimal digits for project. 0082 → `82`, 0083 → `83` all fine through 99. At project 100+, the convention breaks (`666666 + 10001 + 01 = 66666610001 01` is 13 chars vs. the UUID's 12-char slot). Iter 101-117 should decide: (i) shift step-UUIDs to 3-digit project prefix at 100 (breaks convention visually but keeps clean structure); (ii) use different prefix template from 100+ (e.g., `66666700NN01..` for 100-199 range); (iii) rethink step-UUID generation entirely. Flag priority for iter 101 or iter 102 — decide before project 100 ships.
- (k) **Iter 100 word count:** ~14,500 words total (0082 ~9,800 + 0083 ~4,700). Well below iter-98's 17,700-word ceiling. 6-step + 4-step pairing fits depth floor cleanly.
- (l) **Milestone observation:** iter 100 is a round number only by artifact of the iteration cadence — not a planned "halfway" moment (halfway to 200 content projects is project 100, not iteration 100). The content-queue pivot at 100 projects remains the real milestone.

## Iter 99 — 2026-04-19 — Content queue +2 — 81/200 (teacherben Education 4-step Sonnet 4.6 beginner, ops_nina Productivity 5-step Opus 4.6 intermediate)

**What shipped.** Appended two projects to `supabase/seed-content-chains.sql`: **0080** teacherben / Education / 4-step Sonnet 4.6 beginner — first-year 9th-grade general-science teacher handed a mandatory school science fair mid-October with 112 students across 5 sections, 8-week runway, zero lab budget, no documentation from the previous teacher (who left over summer), and a December 12 fair date — sat down Saturday morning with Sonnet 4.6 to build the full operational package. Pass 1 project framework — 4 archetypes explicitly calibrated to the zero-budget constraint (observational/natural-science / kitchen-home-chemistry / survey-human-behavior / capped-device-engineering with a <\$10 hardware-store ceiling) + topic-approval rubric with 5 all-must-be-yes gates (can-you-do-this-for-<\$10 / finish-data-in-10-days-excluding-Thanksgiving / explain-in-one-sentence / 3-variables-1-measurement / if-it-fails-can-you-still-write-it-up-as-what-I-learned) + banned-topics list (live animals / open flames / purchased kits / parent-PhD-level-required / volcanoes explicitly) + design-for-the-40th-percentile-kid load-bearing framing. Pass 2 8-week calendar with three named gates (Week 2 topic gate hard-cutoff-at-Week-3 / Week 5 DATA GATE "this is the week that will blow up" / Week 7 poster gate) + weekly teacher-task column (parent email day 1 with judge signup / weekly spreadsheet update / running "kids I'm worried about" list peaking at 10-15 in week 5 / three teacher-tasks-that-will-tank-you-if-missed) + Thanksgiving-week as buffer-only no-new-work + explicit pre-commit-to-holding-week-5-gate rule ("you will be tempted to give one more week to 8 kids — don't"). Pass 3 judging rubric — 5 criteria (question clarity / method / data / conclusion / ownership) on 0-4 scale = 20 total with award-buckets gold-17-20 / silver-13-16 / bronze-9-12 / participation-0-8 + explicit omission rationale for creativity-visual-appeal-difficulty (taste criteria not judge-able criteria) + judge briefing one-pager + 20-minute calibration exercise (3 sample projects / 7-min silent scoring / 8-min reveal-and-discuss / 2-min round-DOWN-default norm) + score-compile rule (2 judges per project / average / >4-point-disagreement = teacher-breaks-tie) + don't-reveal-running-averages rule to prevent unconscious recalibration. Pass 4 failure safety net — simpler-track path (3-slide presentation / half-credit / 1-panel-poster-not-tri-fold / DO-NOT-cluster-simpler-track-stations-on-fair-day) + conversation script for Week-5/7 gate misses ("I don't want you to try and end up with nothing — there's another option called simpler-track...") + what-NOT-to-do list (no "failed"/"behind"/"giving up" vocabulary / not in front of classmates / kid-first-then-parent) + run-day physical layout (6×17 gym tables / painter's-tape numbering / 8:50am calibration / 9-11:30 judging / 11:30-12:15 score compile + tiebreakers / 12:15-12:30 awards / 12:30-1:45 parents walk / 2pm cleanup) + "something went wrong" plan (judge no-show redistribute / poster-fell-apart → spare tri-folds at teacher table / parent-escalates-on-score → walk-through-rubric-never-re-score-on-fair-day / kid-cries → 5-min back-room reset / teacher-fried-at-11am → eat at 10:45 + standby colleague) + Monday-after 20-min debrief + thank-volunteer-judges-within-48-hours + write-one-page-how-to-run-this-fair-doc. Result content notes 97 full projects completed on time, 11 simpler-track finishes, 4 incompletes (extended absences, handled separately), two families told him "most substantive conference they'd had with a teacher in years"... wait that's the 0069 feedback; for 0080: two parents told him post-fair "best science fair the school has done" vibe, judges scored within 1 point across calibration, the "design for 40th-percentile kid" framing shaped every subsequent decision. **0081** ops_nina / Productivity / 5-step Opus 4.6 intermediate — 50-person creative agency (12-20 active clients, 6-week to 6-month engagements) where three different clients in Feb-Mar 2026 told the exec sponsor "no one told me that" with wildly different specific content (invoice cadence / revision math / team-email access) but identical failure pattern; Nina got 8 weeks to rebuild onboarding. Pass 1 audit design — 3-group interview scripts (PMs: walk-me-through-kickoff / what-you-tell-verbally-not-in-doc / what-you-defer / clients: walk-me-through-first-two-weeks / what-you-wished-we'd-told-you-earlier / when-did-you-first-feel-like-you-got-it as best-single-question / execs: the-escalations-you've-been-taking / which-PMs-you-trust-without-checking) + confidentiality protocol (no recording / handwritten notes / patterns-not-people promise in writing + spoken in opening) + bias mitigation (interview-most-careful-PM-FIRST to recalibrate baseline / write-5-expected-patterns-before-interviews to catch fishing) + 1-page "what I heard" shared with all 6 interviewees before building-anything. Pass 2 categorization framework — 4 root-cause types (surprise = client acted without knowing / deferred = PM knew and waited / missing commitment = said verbally never written / conflicting = two people at agency told different versions) + test-flowchart-per-category + fix-shape-per-category + prediction 2-3 surprise / 3-4 deferred / 3-4 missing / 1-2 conflicting (matched Nina's actual: 3/4/3/1) + the-common-fix-shape ("named artifacts + explicit triggers, not train-PMs-better") + discipline to collapse-leaks-into-commitments rather than add-commitment-per-leak. Pass 3 rebuild — 11 communication commitments in a spec table (trigger / owner / medium / deadline) covering 9 root-cause targets with intentional belt-and-suspenders double-coverage on revision-rounds (#1 engagement letter + #6 standalone revision-rounds artifact restated week 3) and invoicing (#1 engagement letter + #5 AP-to-AP email) + "artifact, not meeting" default rule + 3 explicit cases where meeting IS right (relationship-building / ambiguous-real-time / concern-raised-needs-to-feel-heard) + the cultural one-liner "when in doubt write it; a written commitment the client can reread beats a meeting the client half-remembers" + 3 pressure-test items (#8 30-day check-in is most-load-bearing-prototype-with-one-PM-first / #10 60-day exec recommit will hit "client didn't want it" hold-the-line / #11 escalation reconciliation is policy-not-frequent-muscle) + what-NOT-to-add list (no mid-week check-in / no completion retro / no day-30 NPS). Pass 4 rollout — NOT-an-all-hands (fait-accompli triggers underground-resistance) + 6-week staged sequence (Week 1 willing-partner Kendra-with-fingerprints-on-spec / Week 2 pilot-new-client-X-4-to-6-weeks / Week 3 skeptical-PM 1:1s with match-a-commitment-to-their-deepest-fear as single-most-load-bearing-move / Week 4 fence-sitter 1:1s / Week 5 PM-team-meeting-framed-as-retro-not-announcement / Week 6 first-non-pilot-PM fence-sitter-chosen-for-early-momentum / Weeks 7-12 gradual fence-sitters-first-skeptics-last retrofit-existing-clients-no) + CEO messaging line ("announcing this before it works is the fastest way to make it not work") + what-NOT-to-say list (process-overhaul / we-had-a-lot-of-leaks / name-individual-PMs-in-writing) + week-3 timing rule (1:1s must happen BEFORE fence-sitters hear about it via whisper network) + v1.0-with-public-commit-to-v2.0-at-60-days for staying-power. Pass 5 60-day watchlist — 5 primary signals (no-one-told-me-that mentions lagging target-0 / commitment-delivery-rate leading target-100%-on-#1-5-≥90%-on-#6-11 / client-response-time-on-first-feedback leading target-<36-hours-median / PM-client-question-hours leading target--30%-vs-baseline / client-NPS-at-day-60 lagging target-median-≥8) + 2 anti-metrics (zero-misses-across-all-PMs = reporting-artifact-or-gaming / +20%-engagement-hours = heavier-not-better) + 90-min day-60 retro ritual (15-min data / 30-min per-commitment walk / 15-min pattern / 20-min v2-decisions-cap-at-3 / 10-min re-commit) + retro hygiene (don't-retro-individual-PMs / hold-retro-even-if-great / write-changes-same-day) + 4 explicit kill conditions (full-revert = anti-metric-2-hit + any-primary-worse-than-baseline / partial-revert = specific-commitment-<40%-across-3+-PMs-AND-4+-PMs-call-it-overhead / stay-the-course = mixed-at-60-is-normal don't-panic-revert / democratic-revert = 4-of-8-PMs-want-to-go-back-don't-argue) + the single most-important rule "if it works don't add more — when a new leak surfaces tighten an existing commitment 80% of the time not add a new one" + day-60 three-paragraph closing-memo to close-the-loop.

**Why this approach (rationale).** Iter 98 follow-up gave clean guidance: (b) 6 categories tied at 7 (Finance / Marketing / Data / Education / Productivity / Personal) — iter 99 should pick from the 7-cluster to keep the 7→8 advance pipeline moving; (c) 6 authors tied at 7 (teacherben / dataraj / ops_nina / sarahgrows / marcusdev / lena_solopreneur) — pick from the 7-pack to keep growing the 8-cluster; (e) 26/26/26 PERFECT — any single model pick within-1 is fine; (f) beginner at 26.6% just below peak, one beginner nudges back toward target; (d) 6-step + 7-step tails at 3 each are moderate, 3-step heavy at 26 — middle-lengths (4-step / 5-step) add spread without forcing. teacherben + ops_nina pairing hits all: 4-step science-fair advances teacherben 7→8 AND Education 7→8 AND is fresh (prior teacherben: differentiated bio 3-step, APUSH DBQ 4-step, IEP prep 4-step, Unit-4 genetics postmortem 4-step, Algebra 2 quadratics 4-step, cellular respiration 3-step, parent-teacher conferences 3-step — zero science-fair, zero running-a-school-event); 5-step onboarding-audit-and-rebuild advances ops_nina 7→8 AND Productivity 7→8 AND is fresh (prior ops_nina: Monday leadership-sync 3-step, capacity-planning memo 4-step, on-call rotation 5-step, 34-meeting audit 3-step, OKR workshop 4-step, project-reset 4-step, year-end comp review 7-step — zero client-onboarding-process, zero audit-then-rebuild-pattern). Model rotation: Sonnet 4.6 for the 4-step science-fair chain (structured logistics with procedure-design work, no heavy reasoning required — Sonnet's voice-plus-craft sweet spot, confirmed best-practice per project-0079 which used Sonnet for ghostwriting in the same voice-plus-structure zone), Opus 4.6 for the 5-step onboarding-rebuild (organizational-dynamics with cross-pass consistency across audit → categorize → redesign → rollout → watchlist — requires holding the same mental model of the 8-PM-agency and the 11-commitment-spec across all 5 passes, and making decisions in pass 4 that reference pass 3's spec specifically; Opus 4.6 is the natural fit for this cross-pass-consistency-with-org-judgment work). Rejected alternatives: (i) 3-step science-fair for teacherben — would collapse archetypes + calendar + rubric + safety-net into fewer passes, losing the distinctness of each phase; 4-step is the natural minimum where the 8-week calendar earns its own pass; (ii) Sonnet for both — would leave Opus 4.6 behind at 26 while other two advance (breaks within-1); (iii) picking dataraj + marcusdev pair in Data + Coding — both strong but Coding already at 8 (no category-advance) and Data category advance is genuinely possible via dataraj BUT choosing teacherben/ops_nina cleans up 2 distinct at-7 categories AND 2 distinct at-7 authors with topic-fresh chains; best efficiency; (iv) 6-step or 7-step chain to advance the thin tail — considered for 0081 but the onboarding-audit pattern genuinely fits 5 passes (audit / categorize / redesign / rollout / measure) and forcing a 6th or 7th pass would add cadence without adding content; chain-length diversity is a light-touch preference not a forcing function; (v) making 0080 intermediate instead of beginner — science-fair-ops is genuinely beginner-accessible (any teacher in the first 3 years of teaching will face this exact problem) and the 27% beginner target is a live constraint. Topic choices: science fair is universal K-12 territory that 80%+ of science teachers will face at some point and the "no documentation, no budget, 8 weeks, 100+ kids" scenario is the specific constraint that makes the content work-LM-out-of-convention — any generic "plan a science fair" would fail the 40th-percentile-kid test; onboarding-audit-then-rebuild is the archetypal operations-manager move and the "3 clients said no one told me that" trigger is concrete enough to anchor the entire 5-pass arc, generalizes to any services business (agency / consulting / law firm / dev shop) where client-communication-leaks are chronic.

Approaching production-readiness pivot at 100 (10 iters away); strongly recommend Drew review before pivot.
- (h) **Quality observation on 0080:** the most load-bearing single sentence in the whole project was Claude's pass-2 line "Week 5 is the week that will blow up" — prediction stated in advance changes how the teacher reads the rest of the calendar, and pre-commits him to holding the gate before he's tired from holding it. Future multi-phase projects should include one prediction-of-future-pain paragraph per phase; it's a light-touch move that changes how the reader internalizes the rest.
- (i) **Quality observation on 0081:** the pass-4 rollout sequence demonstrated a pattern worth repeating in future change-management projects — "find the one PM whose fear you know and address it explicitly" as the single most load-bearing move. This beats generic rollout playbooks that say "identify champions" because it tells you WHICH person and WHICH fear, which is where most rollouts fail (champions chosen on enthusiasm alone flake; champions chosen because their fear is addressed commit).
- (j) **Step-ID allocation confirmed working at project 80+.** The hex-like 2-digit-project + 2-digit-step pattern (`666666XXYY01..YYZZ`) handles the 80-99 range cleanly (80, 81 are normal 2-digit decimals); continues to work through 99; at 100+ the convention will need extension (3 digits at the project slot = `...1000101` or equivalent). Flag for iter 100: decide renaming-convention before hitting 100 OR confirm current pattern tolerates 3-digit project codes. Reading the convention literally, `666666990101` works but `6666661000101` adds a character; worth a brief check at iter 99 or iter 100.
- (k) **Iter 99 word count:** ~9,500 words total (0080 ~4,300 + 0081 ~5,200) — comfortably below iter-98's 17,700-word ceiling. Confirms that 4-step + 5-step pairing fits the 15-25-min depth floor cleanly without hitting the long-chain ceiling.

## Iter 98 — 2026-04-19 — Content queue +2 — 79/200 (priya_creates Design 8-step Opus 4.7 advanced, emwriter Writing 3-step Sonnet 4.6 intermediate)

**What shipped.** Appended two projects to `supabase/seed-content-chains.sql`: **0078** priya_creates / Design / 8-step Opus 4.7 advanced — IA refactor of a 110-person ops-tooling startup's admin-panel settings surface (47 toggles piled under one gear-icon accordion, no URLs, no search, single column stretches to 4800px on mobile, "where is X" is the #1 CX inbound). Pass 1 principles doc with an explicit one-sentence purpose + 5 principles (hierarchy-before-search / one-setting-has-one-home / named-URLs-per-leaf / mobile-is-first-class / destructive-is-slow) + explicit out-of-scope list (not feature-discovery / not dashboard / not permissions debugger / not API replacement / not onboarding) engineered to win week-3 scope debates by pointing at the list rather than re-arguing. Pass 2 user research plan — 5 interviews across daily / weekly / first-time admin tiers with 4-block 30-min script (context → open-ended recall → card sort → forced ranking), explicit anti-leading-question list, Maze unmoderated tree test as follow-on after taxonomy draft (not before), and the physical-affinity-mapping rule (printing quotes + moving them around disrupts pattern-match-to-what-I-already-believe). Pass 3 taxonomy proposal — 6 sections (Organization / Access & Identity / Billing / Notifications / Integrations / Advanced) mapping all 47 settings with 0 drops and 0 duplication, contested-settings resolution (API keys → Integrations not Access, Audit log → Advanced, Slack-for-notifications → Notifications with cross-link to Integrations), 4 named anti-traps (no "General" / no "Preferences" / no "Security" top-level / no "Team") each with specific rationale. Pass 4 nav spec — 240px left rail + right pane, `/settings` redirects to first section (no dashboard landing), URL convention with named leaves + entity routes (`/settings/access/roles/:slug`), breadcrumbs on level-2+ leaves only (level-1 "Settings › Organization" is noise), empty / loading / 403 leaf states, section ordering by frequency-plus-criticality not alphabetical. Pass 5 findability — settings-scoped ⌘K with synonym list (SSO ← saml/okta-login/google-login, API keys ← pat/access tokens/api tokens), max 6 results visible, max 3 hand-curated cross-links per leaf, "recents not favorites" ship-A-then-B decision (favorites feature has high cost for 10-20% power-user slice that local-storage recents serves 80% as well at 5% cost), hierarchy-before-search load-bearing rule ("if search exceeds 25% of navigation that's a taxonomy red flag"). Pass 6 mobile 375px 3-view pattern (section list → leaf list → leaf content) with deep-link-synthesizes-back-stack rule, sticky save button full-width, list-cards-not-horizontal-scrolling-tables for members, no hamburger / no bottom-nav / no desktop-layout-squeezed, real-device-not-responsive-viewer test mandate. Pass 7 migration plan — redirect table with 10+ explicit old→new mappings as repo-config (not scattered middleware), 30-day dismissable "moved to X" banner, 3-channel comms cadence (in-product 7 days ahead + admin email T-3 & T+1 + docs + canned-support-ticket templates updated day-of), enterprise white-glove CSM calls, 4-stage feature-flag rollout (internal / 5% / 25% / 100%) with flag-flip rollback. Pass 8 30-day watchlist with 7 metrics + specific thresholds + action-triggers (findability-tickets target 50% reduction / time-to-first-edit target 40% drop / navigation-source-mix target >60% left-rail-click / mobile-session-rate stable-or-up / per-setting ticket concentration <8% / bookmark-URL 404 rate <0.5% / session-time-UP-is-discovery-not-regression), 4 anti-metrics (settings page views / bounce-rate / scroll-depth / click-heatmaps-as-KPI), quarterly durability test (4 questions — any new un-fitting settings? leaf with >15 controls? Advanced grew >50%? old-redirect traffic spike?), post-mortem-even-if-it-went-well discipline. Result content notes post-launch: support tickets tagged `settings-findability` dropped from 23/week to 6/week (74% reduction), median time-to-first-edit 42s→11s, session-time UP 20% (expected — discovery not lostness), session-time-up baseline saved as known-good-signal on watchlist. **0079** emwriter / Writing / 3-step Sonnet 4.6 intermediate — ghostwriting a Series-A CI-observability startup's shutdown announcement (DataPilot, $12M raised 2022, 38 employees, 4 years, couldn't hit CAC payback under 24 months at fundraise scale, board voted wind-down with ~14 months runway remaining → rare ~$3M return to investors). First draft from founder was 1,400 words, led with macro-environment blame, thanked investors before customers, didn't state the shutdown date until paragraph 7. Pass 1 5-section shape (news first in 60-word opener with date / 200-word ownership-not-blame / 200-word customer logistics with exact dates + data-export tool + named-person-contact + recommended alternative / 150-word thank-yous employees-first-then-customers-then-investors / 60-word founder-next) + tone principles (own-without-performing / no-hedging / no-consolation-prize / no-business-speak / three-audience-read customers-then-employees-then-investors-then-tech-community) + what-to-cut list targeting macro paragraphs and silver-lining and "we would be remiss" padding + subject-line-is-the-news rule. Pass 2 surgical critique of emwriter's 680-word draft — 6 flagged sentences with rationalizing-vs-owning diagnosis (Flag 1: "which is important to us" = self-soothing clause delete / Flag 2: "that's on you" customer-credit = over-humble deflection rewrite / Flag 3: "We tried three DIFFERENT ICPs. NONE got us..." = defensive-padding trim to "We tried three ICPs and couldn't get CAC payback" / Flag 4: "in a board meeting" agency-shift → "I made the call with the board's support" / Flag 5: investor-paragraph middle sentence re-surfacing $3M = fishing for acknowledgment, delete / Flag 6: "instead of abruptly" implicit contrast with other founders' shutdowns, delete / Flag 7: "approximately $3M" legal-hedge → "roughly $3M") + state-what's-working-first discipline to prevent overcorrection + public-severance-disclosure pros/cons (lean public if above-norm) + emotional-note-to-ghostwriter "don't let silver lining back in." Pass 3 publish cascade — concentric-circles timing (T-2 weeks board + lead investors phone-not-email / T-1 week top-15-customer pre-brief personal-from-founder + press-under-embargo-only-if-existing-relationships / T-1 day 5pm all-hands Zoom with 38 people + 5:45pm written-follow-up-that-is-the-record + 6:30pm leadership 1:1s + DO-NOT-publish-overnight; Publish-day 6am remaining-customer-email + 6:15 ex-employee heads-up + 6:30 internal-Slack-with-9am-embargo + 9am public post + founder's personal LinkedIn + 9:15 Twitter/X + 9:30 employee-share + 10am-2pm founder-personal-customer-replies; Day+1 top-15-follow-up + internal Friday-PM all-hands-check-in; ongoing weekly customer + team updates) + silence-on-Day-2 rule (no thanks-for-kind-messages / no retweets-of-supportive-comments — signal the post WAS the comm not a performance) + what-the-cascade-prevents checklist (employee-learns-from-Twitter prevented / key-customer-hears-from-reporter prevented / narrative-shaped-by-speculation prevented / severance-seen-first-in-legal-doc prevented). Result content notes the published post ran 620 words (tight for genre where 1200+ bloat is standard), 2 customers wrote privately saying comms made them want to work with founder at next company, one investor wrote "best wind-down comms in 18 years of VC."

**Why this approach (rationale).** Iter 97 follow-up gave clean guidance: (b) author floor now 7 uniform, freeing topic / chain-length / model priorities over strict author rotation; (c) beginner tier at 27.3% (target met, tier-agnostic OK); (e) 8-step tail was thinnest at 2 chains — opportunistic long-chain pick explicitly flagged as natural move; (f) model rotation 25/26/25 meant Sonnet + Opus 4.7 picks retighten toward perfect 26/26/26 balance. priya_creates + emwriter pairing hits all four: 8-step IA-refactor fills the tail + is fresh ground in priya's corpus (prior priya: research synthesis 4-step, dashboard pre-crit 3-step, empty-state audit 4-step, onboarding 3-step, brand 3-step, earlier projects 3-step, button audit 3-step — zero 8-step, zero info-architecture); emwriter shutdown-announcement is fresh ground (prior emwriter: B2B fintech launch 4-step, Q4 all-hands 5-step, viral-complaint 4-step, annual review 3-step, conference keynote 3-step, startup blog 3-step, partnership announcement 3-step, goodbye email 3-step — zero shutdown / crisis-comms). Model rotation: Opus 4.7 for the 8-step IA chain (capability justified — 8 passes of design judgment with cross-pass consistency required, recursive self-critique in pass 5 to resist "just add search" seductive-shortcut, pushback-on-user's-instinct in pass 5 where founder would normally want favorites feature and Claude recommended against it), Sonnet 4.6 for the 3-step shutdown-ghostwrite (structured-judgment-plus-craft-copy work — Sonnet's voice-and-restraint fit the ghostwriting-editor role cleanly; pass 2 critique required surgical-not-sweeping feedback which is the Sonnet sweet spot; tier: intermediate not beginner because rationalizing-vs-owning distinction requires craft). Topic choices: IA refactor is evergreen design-leadership territory anyone rebuilding settings at a B2B SaaS will encounter; shutdown-announcement is the morbid-but-important territory 2026 has a lot of (2024-2025 funding crunch shutdowns accelerating into 2026) and most founders handle it badly because no one taught them how — the "your job is to cut 80% of the explanation" framing transfers.

## Iter 97 — 2026-04-19 — Content queue +2 — 77/200 (marcusdev Coding 4-step Opus 4.6 intermediate, lena_solopreneur Personal 3-step Sonnet 4.6 beginner)

**What shipped.** Appended two projects to `supabase/seed-content-chains.sql`: **0076** marcusdev / Coding / 4-step Opus 4.6 intermediate — Next.js 14 + pnpm workspace where splitting `packages/core` as a shared TS lib caused cold `tsc --noEmit` to balloon 30s → 3m50s, CI type-check timing out at the 5-min job cap. Pass 1 diagnostic plan ranking the five likely causes in frequency order (paths-globs / skipLibCheck / include-patterns / recursive-generics / project-references) + Step-A `--extendedDiagnostics` for aggregate timing and file count + Step-B `--listFiles | wc -l` + `grep node_modules | wc -l` + Step-C `--generateTrace` + `@typescript/analyze-trace` + Step-D project-references-check, with explicit "don't run C blind — it's 50-500MB and the analyzer takes minutes, aim it once A/B narrow the suspect" guidance + 1-hr suspect-identification budget; calls out parse-dominated-vs-check-dominated as the discriminator between extra-files and heavy-types. Pass 2 reads the raw diagnostic output — file count jumped 3,500 → 11,847 with 8,426 in `node_modules` + 712K lines of definitions + Check time 148s/64% as the smoking gun — prescribes `awk -F/ '{print $1"/"$2"/"$3}' | sort | uniq -c | sort -rn | head -20` to bin the dominant contributor and predicts the fix will be a paths-glob that matches `../../packages/core/node_modules/*`, with explicit teachable-moment that a trace is overkill here (this is an extra-files problem, not a slow-type problem — different tools for different failure modes). Pass 3 user confirms: `paths: @core/*: [../../packages/core/src/*, ../../packages/core/node_modules/*]` was pulling 4,218 `@aws-sdk/.pnpm` files, and analyze-trace found `Deep<UserConfigSchema>` (recursive mapped type over a 200-field Zod schema) at 4.4s/instance — Claude explains the teachable rule ("paths is a workspace-alias layer ABOVE Node's resolver, not a package-storage hint — every time someone uses a wildcard in paths pointing at a directory that could contain real source files, they set up this trap"), walks through why recursive mapped types over deep objects are ~O(n²) in the checker, and gives 3 fix options for the recursive type (don't use / precompute single alias for caching / `as const` at value level). Pass 4 ships a 40-line `scripts/tsc-perf-guard.sh` that parses `--extendedDiagnostics` "Total time" and fails CI over 90s (`TSC_PERF_THRESHOLD_S` env-overridable) + GitHub Actions yaml wiring + explicit "resist setting 45s to be strict — you'll get false positives on loaded runners and start adding `continue-on-error`" anti-false-positive rule + 3 month-2 tweaks (rolling 2-week average threshold / PR-not-just-main enforcement / bump-as-code-change-for-review governance) + closing postmortem note that this case had two independent causes (paths-glob + recursive-type) and you only find both if you run `--extendedDiagnostics` AND `analyze-trace`, because they measure different failure modes. **0077** lena_solopreneur / Personal / 3-step Sonnet 4.6 beginner — 32yo solo consultant running one-woman strategy practice from home at $140K/yr variable income, friend's rescue referred her to a 3yo terrier-mix (Mabel) whose listed profile matched her life, meet-and-greet Saturday, 5 years of "I'll adopt when more settled" deferral behind the decision. Pass 1 specific-to-her pros/cons (NOT generic lists) naming working-from-home-as-structural-fit + Mabel's profile-match as signal, then 4 "reasons I hesitate that aren't good reasons" with punchy reframes (waiting-to-be-more-settled = deferral-not-planning / partner-kids-moves = bring-along-not-reason-to-wait / worry-about-being-bad-owner = evidence-of-conscientiousness-not-unfitness / big-commitment-abstract = different-question-from-specific-dog), 3 legit reasons to say no (no credible-backup-plan / $3-5K vet scenario panic / meet-and-greet fit miss), a 7-question shelter script leading with "actual surrender reason in family's own words" (softening listings is common), separation-anxiety-testing as the #1 predictor of return, and closing self-test "am I excited-and-nervous, or talking-myself-into-it — trust the distinction." Pass 2 year-1 budget line-by-line: $865 setup (adoption $350, crate/bed/harness/bowls/gates/cleaner/initial vet) + $3,650 ongoing annual (food $600, treats $180, vet wellness $350, heartworm+flea $260, dental-cleaning-pro-rated $400, pet insurance $480 flagged STRONGLY RECOMMEND for income-volatile owners, grooming $360, boarding $880 initial number revised to $1,500 in Round 3, toys/license/chews), three emergency scenarios ($600-1,200 minor / $2,500-5,000 moderate surgical ~1-in-3 lifetime rate / $5-12K+ catastrophic ~5% lifetime rate) with insurance-out-of-pocket math, the core reframe "insurance converts variable risk to fixed monthly cost — which is exactly what someone with variable income should be doing across most risk categories," $1,500 envelope pre-fund rule with don't-carry-pet-emergency-on-credit-card failure-mode naming, and bad-month worked example showing $180 real hit with plan vs. credit-card spiral without. Pass 3 3-layer travel plan (Primary: in-home boarding with named $45-65/night person — "identify 1-2 candidates THIS WEEK" / Backup: commercial facility pre-toured with 1-night trial at month 2 — "do NOT make your first commercial use a 7-day trip" / Floor: $25-35 dog-walker visits for short trips and sick-day coverage pre-negotiated — "do not wait until you're sick to figure this out"), 27-nights/year math correcting the Round-2 boarding line upward to $1,500, month-1-or-2 dry-run boarding rationale, 4 first-30-day deal-breakers (severe SA not improving by day 21-28 = behaviorist+rescue call / unflagged reactivity = 4-6 trainer sessions then reassess / food-aggression-to-humans = behaviorist IMMEDIATELY not "after a few weeks" / week-4-honest-feeling — "do I look forward to seeing her when I walk in the door"), 10-half-capacity-working-days calendar block protecting against the "work around it" failure mode, and closing "returning a dog that isn't a fit is not a failure; forcing yourself to keep one you don't love is" to pre-empt sunk-cost paralysis. Result content captures the post-adoption outcome (adopted 3 weeks later) and the one thing the plan got wrong (underestimating first-2-weeks work disruption).

**Design rationale.** Iter 95 follow-ups gave a near-forced pairing: (b) three categories tied-low at 6 (Marketing/Productivity/Personal) → pick two to close spread; (c) four authors at 6-peat floor (lena/sarahgrows/marcusdev/ops_nina) → advance two; (e) chain-length tails thin at 7-step/8-step (both at 2), 6-step at 3 → commit to a 6+-step chain this iter per explicit (j) follow-up; (f) model rotation perfect 24/24/24 → any model works on topic fit; (b) beginner tier at 26.0% needing nudge toward 27% target → pick 1 beginner topic. ## Iter 95 — 2026-04-19 — Content queue +2 — 73/200 (cto_derek Coding 5-step Opus 4.6 advanced, priya_creates Design 3-step Sonnet 4.6 intermediate)

**What shipped.** Appended two projects to `supabase/seed-content-chains.sql`: **0072** cto_derek / Coding / 5-step Opus 4.6 advanced — CTO at 45-person HIPAA health-tech planning Postgres 14 → 17 major version upgrade on 1.4TB primary cluster with 287GB patient_encounters + 60GB audit_log tables before 14 EOL in November 2026. Pass 1 scope-and-constraints inventory (10 numbers to pin down before path selection — size-by-top-10-tables / p99-latency-baseline / connection-counts / replication-lag-baseline / extension-inventory / 6-quirky-services-behavior / audit-log-vacuum-state / PITR-drill-<2h / weekend-exclusions / named-rollback-DRI-with-backup) + explicit NOT-this-window deferral list (tablespace moves / schema changes / non-required extension bumps / PgBouncer version bump / app deploys Fri-Sun / SSL rotation / topology changes / tuning overhauls / replica-promotion tests) + CM-board 1-page memo format with pushback-on-framing that measurement and pre-commitment aren't the same thing and both are needed. Pass 2 three-path comparison with honest tradeoff table: pg_upgrade (45-90min downtime / 94-min PITR-only rollback / no pre-cutover validation), logical replication blue-green (10-30min cutover / instant PgBouncer-flip rollback / days of pre-validation against real traffic / 2x storage + DDL-not-replicated + sequence-cutover complexity), pg_dump+restore disqualified at 1.4TB (6-12h). Recommendation Path B grounded in HIPAA rollback-speed dominance under 4h RTO + self-counter-argument on sequence-cutover and DDL-not-replicated pitfalls requiring 72h DDL freeze + schema-diff verification script blocking go-live + pushback-on-framing that Path B's cost is operational-ops BEFORE cutover night (cluster stand-up, replication setup, schema-diff script, rehearsal) — NOT cheaper night but much-cheaper night bought with 2 weeks expensive day work. Pass 3 full minute-by-minute runbook: Phase 0 T-14d prep (17 cluster provision + initial sync 18-36h monitored via pg_stat_subscription / schema-diff script every 30min from T-72h / DDL freeze T-72h with #eng-changes broadcast + pipeline disabled / sequence-cutover script with +10000 safety buffer / staging PITR <2h verified / 9-participant on-call rotation confirmed), Phase 1 Saturday dry-run T-24h (any step >1.5x estimate = fix+re-rehearse, abort real cutover if dry-run not clean by Sat 6pm — reschedule, no heroics), Phase 2 cutover-night with T-30min preflight (lag<1s, schema-diff clean, 17-health-yellow=stop, 9-on-bridge-else-delay-then-abort) / T+0 drain (pause-pools-not-disconnect, 60s wait, force-terminate idle-in-transaction >10s where quirky services surface, abort if >20 sessions remain) / T+5 lag=0 verify + sequence script (checkpoint 1: lag≠0 OR script error = rollback while pools paused) / T+10 PgBouncer flip via config-file change + reload-not-restart (first 30s: >5% errors 15s = rollback) / T+15 smoke 8 tests 3min (checkpoint 2: 8/8 proceed / 7/8 retry-once flake-rule / <7 rollback) + HIPAA audit-log write test specifically / T+25 ANALYZE top-10 parallel + EXPLAIN on 5 hot queries vs baseline (checkpoint 3: >3x regression opens rollback-consideration, 2x suspicious-not-auto) / T+60 traffic ramp + 30min p99 watch / T+90 declare complete, 14 read-only reference 7 days, DRI watches 4 more hours. Phase 3 rollback levels: minor=retry-flake / hard=PgBouncer config revert + reload + resume <3min no-data-loss WAL-current-at-drain / deep (>1hr post-cutover) = pre-staged reverse-subscription 17→14 activate+catch+flip 30-60min with data-delta HIPAA-audit-trail tested. Abort-not-rollback: past 4am / CM-unreachable-DRI / critical monitoring down at T-30min. Pass 4 10-gate go/no-go spec for CM board with default-NO-GO burden-of-proof on green not red: G1 dry-run <1.5x budget every phase / G2 schema-diff 144 consecutive clean runs over 72h / G3 replication lag <1s sustained 24h / G4 PITR drill <2h staging / G5 sequence-cutover verified end-to-end + post-flip no-PK-collision test / G6 9-person on-call with backups + time-zones / **G7 rollback decision-maker owned by VPE NOT DRI** — independence from DRI as structural firebreak against emotional-investment bias, single most-undervalued item on list / G8 synthetic-page monitoring test within 48h / G9 deferral list zero scope additions / G10 customer-comms + HIPAA disclosure legal sign-off. Decision Thu 5pm all-green → CM ratify Thu 6pm, single-red = next weekend no-debate, yellow-with-mitigation case-by-case full-board default-NO-GO. Anti-pattern to reject "9/10 tenth is minor let's proceed" — tenth bites. Meta: silence-defaults-no-go prevents "couldn't-find-reason-to-stop-so-went" + retrain team that NO-GO is normal outcome not failure. Pass 5 post-cutover monitoring spec split Window-1 72h (every-4h auto + every-12h human) 7 metrics with thresholds — p99-latency-top-5 within 1.2x baseline yellow 2x red fix-via-ANALYZE / error-rate-per-service 1.1x yellow 1.5x red fix-via-pool-restart / WAL-generation 1.3x investigate / async-replica-lag <2s throughput-regression-signal / autovacuum-activity 2x work-volume-tune since 17 defaults differ from 14 / connection-count 1.1x either-way / **HIPAA audit-log write rate ≥0.95x baseline — DROP = reportable emergency alert at 0.90x** — and Window-2 day-4-10 slow-burn (3 categories: plan-regression watchlist 30-50 queries from slow-query log daily EXPLAIN catches JIT-threshold changes in day-4 not week-3 / autovacuum bloat pgstattuple daily on top-10 patient_encounters is watch / dead-tuple-vs-autovacuum-completion rate leading indicator of 2-3 week performance cliff). 7d-close criteria: retire 14 only after all metrics stable + no >1.5x plan regressions + normal bloat + 18 services pool equilibrium + 14 idle-reachable-7d + final PITR. Keep 14 snapshot 90 days HIPAA retention. Day-4+ regression procedure: scope → quantify → escalate rollback only if >20% traffic OR 24h fix-forward fails OR HIPAA-critical-path — deep rollback via reverse-replication catchup + PgBouncer flip with data-delta compliance write-up; post-retro within 5 days. Meta: night-of catches obvious failures, week-of catches non-obvious; teams skipping 7-day window = databases fine until day-11 complaint. **0073** priya_creates / Design / 3-step Sonnet 4.6 intermediate — senior designer at 120-person B2B SaaS auditing 47 accumulated button variants across 3 product teams / 3 codebases. Pass 1 audit method on 3 axes NOT visual-appearance (opinion-vs-opinion stuck, scoring = data-vs-data): semantic-purpose 0-3 (fills distinct role no-other-covers=3, role-also-by-1-other=2 merge-candidate, role-by-2+-others=1 drift, no-clear-role=0) via standard SaaS roles primary-action/secondary/destructive/tertiary-nav/specialized + scan 3 real usage sites per variant via grep imports 1-2hrs for 47 / usage-volume 0-3 terciles via code-refs grep + runtime telemetry 30-day renders (Amplitude/Mixpanel) or code-refs-alone with flagged methodology limitation don't-fake-confidence / accessibility 0-3 via axe-core + manual keyboard-focus (WCAG-AA-all-states / AA-contrast-focus-issues-elsewhere / fails-contrast-OR-missing-focus / multi-fails) with focus-state screenshots since designers-engineers disagree until side-by-side. Composite 0-9 with keep-7-9 / review-5-6 / collapse-3-4 / deprecate-0-2. Why works in dread-conversations: lead can't say "my button special" against score, can only say "semantic score wrong" = data argument re-read and adjust = productive; a11y axis = compliance-adjacent not taste; usage volume = cover for deprecating low-use-emotional-attachment. Artifact: audit spreadsheet with columns variant-name / file-path / semantic-score+role / usage-score+count / a11y-score+failures / composite / recommendation — share with 3 leads BEFORE Pass 2 spec so scoring becomes shared consensus-on-data before drafting. Pushback on "reproducible same scores in a year" framing: semantic-purpose is judgment, two designers score borderline differently; what's reproducible is the PROCESS (same-sources-same-rubric-same-artifacts) where disagreements show on specific rows not overall frame = more valuable than false objectivity. Pass 2 6 canonicals named by semantic role: btn-primary (one per surface the-one-thing, competing-primaries defeat purpose, 6 interactive states) / btn-secondary (same-surface alternate, squint-test must feel less emphasized) / btn-destructive (irreversible-delete/revoke, never fires without confirmation modal, semantic-role IS "irreversible" not "red") / btn-tertiary (link-styled low-emphasis inline+nav, NOT primary form actions even if minimal aesthetic) / btn-icon (dense UI toolbars/rows, MUST aria-label + tooltip, NOT ambiguous icons) / btn-split (primary + dropdown-alternates Save+close+new+draft, keyboard-navigable focus-trapped escape-to-close, reserve for multi-option cases). All with 4.5:1 contrast + focus ring + aria-disabled. Migration map 3 categories: direct-map 17/47 (PrimaryBtn/MainButton/ActionButton/SubmitBtn → btn-primary etc find-replace + parity check), style-fix 14/47 minor padding/hover review with surface-owning team, deprecate 16/47 composite ≤2 removed. Per-variant row in map: current→canonical→type→sites→owner→hours. Escape-hatch governance preventing re-drift: btn-novel slot + 48h async review by Priya + 1-other-designer with 2-sentence justification PR + 2 outcomes absorbed-into-canonical-with-tweak OR genuinely-novel-4-week-observation period then stays-custom if stable + promotes-to-7th-canonical if 2+ teams surface similar need. Words-do-governance-work: don't call it "custom" (implies default-is-use-it), call btn-novel or btn-exception (implies default-is-canonical-deviate-only-for-genuinely-new). Pass 3 rollout to 3 product leads without turf war: sequence counterintuitive — skeptical-lead FIRST (Team B "I-just-need-ship") — sell hard case first → easier leads see skeptical peer bought in = social proof accelerates; sell easy first → skeptical feels fait-accompli entrenches; approach Team B don't bring full spec bring audit spreadsheet ask for input on their team's scoring frame "want to get data right before proposing" = their fingerprints on scoring = consolidation flows from data they co-authored. Second cooperative lead "Team B reviewed scoring here's where we landed" = cross-team-effort not central-mandate. Emotional register shifts from "deprecated" to "recognized". 5 pre-written objections: engineering-work-unplanned → team-owned-schedule + savings-on-maintenance-after / my-variant-needs-to-stay → walk-through, genuine-semantic → 7th-canonical via observation, style-diff → fold into canonical / slow-us-down → maintenance-faster ship-wise-no-hard-deadline / central-design-taking-control → audit-with-your-input + your-implementations-as-references + escape-hatch + recalibrate-if-stops-feeling-true / penalty-if-no-migrate → none rather-land-than-ship-on-deadline. Timeline W0 audit-reviewed → W1 3 1:1s in sequence → W2 follow-up → W3 written-commitment public-kickoff → W4-9 team-by-team migration → W10 retro. **THE MOVE:** let ONE team OWN one canonical's reference implementation (Team C's destructive) — single highest-value move signals not-central-takeover + best-implementations-recognized + distributed-ownership → teams become advocates defend don't push-back. Meta "landing > date" test: if lead says "slammed 3 weeks can push?" answer "yes no problem" — if "well I hoped" you don't believe framing; willingness-to-push makes leads feel safe engaging.

Picked Postgres 14→17 major version upgrade for 0072 because: (a) fresh topic — prior Derek corpus (0009 PHI RFC / 0019 18-mo roadmap / 0050 service mesh RFC / 0064 blameless retro) has zero database-ops or production-cutover content, closest adjacency is 0064's 3h payment-outage retro but that's backward-looking post-incident vs 0072 forward-looking planned-change; (b) 5-step is the right chain length — scope / path / runbook / gate / monitoring decomposes naturally at 5, compressing to 4 drops either the go/no-go gate pass or monitoring window (both load-bearing), expanding to 6 would fragment one pass into two without adding; (c) Opus 4.6 is the right capability match because the runbook has multi-pass multi-branch decision logic (abort triggers with recovery procedures per step, rollback cascade hard→deep, 72h-vs-7d window differentiation) that Sonnet would produce more mechanically; (d) HIPAA context carries forward from 0009 giving continuity without repetition; (e) Postgres 14→17 is genuinely realistic for the 2026-04 timeline — 14 released 2021, EOL Nov 2026 aligns, conservative health-tech shops lag 2-3 versions. **References consulted.** Content-queue iteration; no external reference fetch per SKILL.md (Content-queue grounding is real Claude generation, not external design aesthetic).
