## Iter 66 — 2026-04-18 — Content queue +2 (Personal 3-step + Education 3-step) — Personal closes to 2, depth-per-category phase fully done

**What shipped.** Appended two real Claude-generated project chains to `supabase/seed-content-chains.sql`, taking the content queue from 19/50 to 21/50. Project 0020: Marcus Chen (marcusdev) — "Should I take the Bay Area FAANG offer? — 3-prompt decision framework for a cross-country move with a family", Personal category, 3 steps, Claude 4.6 Opus, intermediate, tools `['Claude','Google Sheets']`, engagement 104/51. Project 0021: Ben Okafor (teacherben) — "Half my 9th-grade bio class bombed the cellular respiration unit test — 3-prompt diagnostic workflow with re-teach plan", Education category, 3 steps, Claude 4.6 Sonnet, beginner, tools `['Claude','Google Classroom','Google Forms']`, engagement 72/38. This iter closes Personal from 1→2 (Lena 0011 camping + Marcus 0020 career decision) — the last 1-project category — meaning the depth-per-category phase is fully done, every category ≥2 projects. Iter 67+ is in any-topic-depth phase, picking categories by audience fit not coverage parity.

**Why this approach.** Two calls this iter. Call 1: Personal closure via marcusdev cross-category. BACKLOG's author/category guide says `lena_solopreneur` (Personal) — a strict read would say pick a new Personal-fit author or cycle Lena again. Reject both: Lena already has 2 projects (Strategy 0007 + Personal 0011), adding a 3rd Lena would create the first 3-peat for the WRONG reason (mechanical rotation, not natural returning-contributor pattern); and creating a new author just for Personal-once would be inflating the authorship roster without narrative purpose. Alternative considered: skip Personal closure entirely and start any-topic-depth with two new topics. Rejected because "closing the floor at 2" is a satisfying ship-point Drew can look at and see as a phase transition — worth the cross-category stretch of using marcusdev for Personal. marcusdev's 0003 was a terse senior-engineer coding refactor; 0020 is the same senior engineer making a career decision with spouse/kids stakes. Same person, same voice, different mode — the kind of real-community repeat that doesn't feel like authorship-roster-padding. Call 2: Ben Okafor's 3rd project. This is the first 3-peat in the content queue. Justified by the teacher-workflow thread being a naturally returning content type (diagnose → re-teach → student-facing → parent-facing is the loop a real teacher runs every unit), not a mechanical author-rotation. 0021 also completes a pedagogical arc across Ben's 3 projects: 0005 was a differentiated bio lesson (instructional design ahead of time), 0012 was a DBQ unit plan (assessment + scaffolded sources), 0021 is the post-assessment diagnostic + re-teach + parent comms (what happens when the unit didn't land). That's a meaningful teacher-workflow sequence, not just "same author picked 3 times." Alternative considered: 3rd cto_derek project or 3rd priya_creates project to establish the depth pattern in a different category. Rejected because Education is where the teacher-workflow thread is strongest and most didactic — it's the category where "same person, different problem" reads clearest.

**On the content itself.** 0020's load-bearing quality move is step-1 Claude pushing back on framing. The user's ask is "help me think about a FAANG offer" — the weak version of this project would have Claude compute $285K→$420K as "+$135K, up to you." Instead step-1 surfaces 9 factors the user missed: sign-on tax treatment (federal AMT exposure on $75K sign-on with RSU vesting), RSU cliff at 12 months creating handcuffs that change the optionality math, CA state tax (13.3% top marginal) eating into the raise, the 3.1% mortgage as a LOCKED-IN ASSET not a sunk cost (selling a 3.1% means buying back at 7.1% later — $200K+ NPV destruction), wife's marketing-manager career ceiling at the Austin office vs Bay-Area reset where she's starting over at 38, kids at K + preschool transition making social cost of the move nontrivial, Bay-Area COL compression eating most of the $135K, one-way-door housing math (selling the Austin house forecloses the option to return), and the "what are you optimizing for" framing question that every career decision hinges on. Step 2's arithmetic is pessimistic-but-defensible with numbers shown: scenario A (full move) $226.4K year-1 spendable after CA tax ($65K hit) + Bay Area COL compression ($48K) + housing delta ($32K mortgage + 28K property tax) + wife's 6-month career gap ($35K assumed 80% probability of finding equivalent role by month 12) = $226.4K — LOWER than scenario C (stay, negotiate staff) $230.2K assuming a 65% probability of the Austin staff promotion hitting, $205K if it doesn't. Critically Claude flags that C's promotion probability is NOT independent of the decision to decline the offer — VP Eng's willingness to push staff may change once he knows Marcus passed on FAANG money, making the 65% a probabilistic range 40-75% not a point estimate. Step 3 is the counter-offer script with realistic-ask menu — $255-270K base + $120-180K RSU refresher + staff title on 6-month clock OR $180-220K base + written commitment to staff within 12 months — not a single ask. 4 failure modes (VP ghosts, VP calls it a bluff, VP accepts partial, VP escalates to peer benchmarking delay) each with a scripted response and a "what do you do when you hang up" decision rule for each branch. This is the quality bar: substantive artifact that a real person in this situation could USE, not a summary of what AI might say.

0021's load-bearing move is step 1's refusal to accept the teacher's framing. The teacher's ask is "help me diagnose what went wrong on this test." The weak version would restate the aggregate 58% average as evidence of "unit-wide struggle" and recommend re-teaching the unit. Instead step 1 reads the per-question score sheet and pinpoints Q13-Q14 (ATP-yield math) as a 30-point-gap that accounts for nearly all the aggregate drop — the vocabulary questions (which the teacher assumed were the weakness) scored 78% and 81%, fine. Q13-Q14 scored 41% and 43%. Claude also flags the 3 on-grade-or-above students who bombed as THE signal: if good students fail specific questions, that's instruction-level not study-effort. This moves the re-teach target from "the unit" to "20 minutes on stoichiometry of ATP yield with a modeled worked problem." Step 2's minute-by-minute plan is load-bearing because the timing is specific enough to actually execute: 5-min opener with the "the responsibility is mine" language anchoring not-blame, 15-min modeled worked problem with think-aloud (Claude scripts the 4 intermediate steps: balanced equation → count CO₂ → count NADH/FADH₂ → multiply by ATP-yield-per-carrier), 20-min paired practice with 5 Q13-Q14-shaped problems and a 5-min graded exit ticket. Day 2 is a group-build poster → gallery walk → 20-min re-quiz with guaranteed replacement-if-higher grading. Step 3's parent email has one really specific craft move: the ownership sentence in paragraph 2 ("the responsibility is mine, and the fix is on me") is load-bearing for parent reception — parents read these emails to find out if the teacher knows what's going on. Claude also makes an explicit targeting call: don't send to above-70% families, it dilutes the signal and invites "why didn't my kid get this email" tension that's solvable by being honest that the re-teach is open to all but the email is targeted.

**References consulted.** Content-queue iter, so no external design reference. Grounding is the quality bar set by project 0001 (Jake's tax estimator) and the 9 intermediate reference points (0002–0019). After iter 66: teacherben at 3 (first 3-peat), 8 authors at 2, marcusdev moves 1→2.

**Follow-ups spotted.**
- **Chain-length drift toward 3-step.** Current distribution is 3/4/2/5/3/4/4/3/5/4/3/4/5/3/4/5/4/3/5/3/3 — ten 3s / seven 4s / five 5s / one 2. Shorter chains are over-represented; the last three projects in a row were 3/3/3 (0018 Design, 0020 Personal, 0021 Education — though 0019 Strategy 5 breaks the streak counting forward, the three newest are all 3s). Iter 67+ should prefer 4-step or 5-step unless the topic genuinely doesn't support it. A single 6-step or 7-step would be especially welcome — BACKLOG explicitly allows up to 8.
- **Difficulty imbalance.** Across 21: 6 beginner / 9 intermediate / 6 advanced. Intermediate is over-indexed; next 2–3 iters should pull one advanced per iter to keep 6/9/6 from tilting further. 0020 was originally considered advanced (financial modeling + probabilistic reasoning) but logged intermediate because the voice and ask are those of a senior engineer who is not a finance specialist — the content is advanced but the author-context is intermediate. Flag: "advanced" has been drifting toward "cto_derek / dataraj specialist topic" in labeling; iter 67 should label a non-specialist at advanced if the work genuinely is.

## Iter 65 — 2026-04-18 — Content queue +2 (Design 3-step + Strategy 5-step) — depth-per-category phase effectively closes

**What shipped.** Appended two real Claude-generated project chains to `supabase/seed-content-chains.sql`, taking the content queue from 17/50 to 19/50. Closes Design and Strategy in the depth-per-category phase — both had been stuck at 1 project since iter 61 (Design) and iter 59 (Strategy). Post-iter-65, the only category still at 1 project is Personal (Lena Morales's 0011 camping trip), but Lena already has 2 total projects because she also owns Strategy 0007 — so the repeat-contributor demonstration for Personal is already satisfied indirectly. The depth-per-category phase is functionally complete; iter 66 pivots to any-topic-depth.

Project `55...5550018`: "Dashboard-redesign pre-crit — 3-pass Claude workflow that caught the critique I couldn't see myself" by Priya Sharma (`priya_creates`, second project — her first was 0010 UX research synthesis → exec deck), Design category, 3 steps, Claude 4.6 Opus, intermediate difficulty. Chain walks a senior product designer's pre-design-review pressure-test on a B2B analytics onboarding redesign (Series B, 43% abandonment on the "connect your first data source" step, 4 sources Segment/Snowflake/Postgres/CSV, 4-step wizard). Step 1 (structural diagnosis) identifies 4 ranked failures with the lead insight being "commitment escalation inverted" — auth is step 2 of an unknown-length flow meaning the highest-trust action precedes the value demo; Claude declines to nitpick UI polish and ranks "fix the commitment escalation first, demo path second, table-mapping-context third, CSV-hidden fourth"; closes with a verify-first flag on by-source funnel split that Priya confirms in step 2 (Snowflake 71% drop, Postgres 65%, Segment 38%, CSV 22%, validating the auth-position thesis). Step 2 (three alternatives with honest tradeoffs) pushes back on Priya's "what is the FIRST thing a user should do" framing — reframes to "what does the user SEE before they're asked to do anything" and delivers three philosophically distinct approaches: A demo-first with CSV as front door, B schema-introspection-with-deferred-mapping, C OAuth-only with warehouse-provider login — each with honest tradeoffs, predicted abandonment number, and engineering-cost honesty. Critically flags Priya's existing design as "possibly A+B blended — worth examining for dilution," which becomes the pivotal note causing her to commit fully to Approach A. Step 3 (multi-persona pre-crit) plays three specific personas in sequence: skeptical staff PM (3 pushbacks, load-bearing one being "what about the 14% who succeed today" → mitigation: persistent top-right "Connect directly" link; plus activation-metric contamination → disaggregate sample-activated vs production-activated; plus 30s-delay issue → defer-and-fix-in-implementation); overloaded platform engineer (3 pushbacks, load-bearing one being "the hosted sample dataset isn't just a file, it's a contract between onboarding and dashboard teams" → mitigation: add sample-dataset ownership section to spec; plus Segment-OAuth clarification defense; plus view-state persistence across sample→real transition deferred with known-open-question flag); data analyst user proxy (2 pushbacks, one fatal in spirit — "a sample CSV demo is theater; I want to paste SQL and see my real data in 30 seconds" — pointed out as the same load-bearing issue as the staff PM's pushback 1 in different clothing, mitigated by the top-right link and v2 commitment). Outcome: design review went 40 minutes (previous on this flow had been 90+), shipped the revised flow, activation on connect-data-source step went from 57% → 73% over six weeks with the biggest single lift from moving auth to step 2-of-2 instead of step 2-of-4.

Project `55...5550019`: "18-month engineering roadmap memo for the board — 5-pass Claude workflow for a Series B health-tech CTO" by Derek Lawson (`cto_derek`, second project — his first was 0009 PHI data boundary RFC), Strategy category, 5 steps, Claude 4.7 Opus, advanced difficulty. Chain walks a Series B health-tech CTO's board-memo rebuild after his Q3 roadmap memo was dismissed as "vague optimism" — stakes include the memo landing in the Series C DD data room. 28 engineers, $18M ARR, runway to Q3 2027. Step 1 (honest-state pass) — Derek pastes his defensive LinkedIn-voiced paragraph plus the known truths (what's shipping, what's stuck, where debt lives, 4 engineers exploring outside roles) and asks Claude to flag where he's still soft. Claude flags 3 places of residual LinkedIn-voicing (sprint hit rate framed as "6 of 8 hit" rather than "2 of 8 missed, both in features depending on scheduling rewrite"; cadence-not-prioritization blind spot; "all 4 Q3 deployments on new architecture" lacking cohort-before-that baseline), 3 places of genuine minimization (scheduling slip framed as scope-wrong when the 9-month slip is actually a decisioning failure he didn't correct; 14% attrition signal needing base-rate anchoring and a ranked read of likely causes not "probably a mix"; observability "in progress for 3 quarters" being a soft way of saying stalled), plus 4 questions a skeptical board reader would ask (attrition vs benchmarks, debt-paydown fraction, feature-to-revenue attach, SOC 2 customer-impact). Delivers a rewritten 2-paragraph current-state section that names the scheduling slip as "a decisioning failure I did not correct at the original delay." Step 2 (three-horizon framing with say-no lists) — drafts H1 committed / H2 planned / H3 scoped with explicit say-no per horizon, then pushes back on three specific things: H1 is over-committed at 42% of remaining-capacity after off-the-top (shrink flagship from 4×3 to 2×3 FTE-months, pre-commit buffer); observability is miscategorized as an H1 "ship" when it's still a decision (H1 weeks 1-4 decide-or-cancel instead); three-path-auth tax needs explicit naming as a conscious H2/H3 trade; also flags SOC 2 report completion pulling forward from H2 to H1 (auditor-timeline check confirms). Step 3 (capacity modeling) — builds the real FTE-months model (168 gross / 84 off-the-top / 84 discretionary allocated 54/15/7/11/13% across feature/reliability/platform/debt/buffer) with 4 perturbation scenarios each pre-committed-costed (scheduling slips 2mo / slips >2mo → observability cancelled breakpoint / flagship ships early / surprise enterprise deal / 2-senior attrition). Names scheduling-rewrite delivery as 21% of discretionary alone (concentration risk) and the buffer as honestly sized for expected-slip not for scheduling at 150% historical. Step 4 (three-member board-objection steelman) — plays operating partner ("what's different from Q3" → commit to explicit memo callout of scope-reset + decide-or-cancel + perturbation-table), independent director ex-CTO ("buffer is a fig leaf" → add footnote disaggregating sizing, name the >50%-slip cancellation breakpoint), growth-investor partner ("where's the Series C narrative" → "you're right, here's the edit": H2 restructures from operational-readiness framing to PHI-safe-platform-as-commercial-asset framing with the head-start-on-compliance moat thesis — the only one of the three where Derek changes the memo itself, not just adds a defense). Meta-observation: memo should lead with commercial thesis then operational plan. Step 5 (final 3-page memo assembly) — thesis paragraph leading, honest current-state section as rewritten in step 1, H1/H2/H3 with say-no lists each + "what's different from Q3" callout, capacity table with buffer footnote, perturbation table, 3 open questions for the board. Outcome: board approved in 35 minutes, memo in Series C DD data room, first investor conversations starting next week.

**Why this approach (content rationale).** Picked Design 3-step + Strategy 5-step to advance three axes: (a) **2nd projects for the two remaining 1-project categories BACKLOG iter 64 explicitly called out** — "Design + Strategy via cto_derek" was the recommended priority next-pair because it closes both categories AND promotes cto_derek from 1→2 projects (he was the only returning-author-from-Coding still at 1). Personal was deferred because Lena already has 2 projects total (0007 Strategy + 0011 Personal), so the depth-per-category goal is effectively already met there. (b) **chain-length variety** — existing lengths post-iter-64: 3/4/2/5/3/4/4/3/5/4/3/4/5/3/4/5/4 (17 projects, five 3s / seven 4s / one 2 / four 5s). Adding 3-step + 5-step gives 6 3s / 7 4s / 1 2 / 5 5s — healthier bottom spread, still no 3-streak of same length. 3-step for 0018 is right because the diagnosis-alternatives-precrit arc is 3 genuinely distinct intellectual steps (adding a 4th "refined recommendation" step would be padding); 5-step for 0019 is earned by the honest-state → horizons-and-say-no → capacity-modeling → board-steelman → memo-assembly arc being 5 genuinely distinct intellectual moves that can't collapse without losing load-bearing content. (c) **model rotation** — post-iter-64: Sonnet 4.6 at 7, Opus 4.6 at 5, Opus 4.7 at 5. This iter uses Opus 4.6 for 0018 (design pre-crit is judgment-heavy but structured; 4.6 was most under-rotated) and Opus 4.7 for 0019 (board-memo work is unambiguously 4.7 territory — residual-voice detection, 3-member steelman with one change-course answer, H2 framing restructure all benefit from 4.7's subtler reasoning). Post-iter-65: Sonnet 4.6 stays at 7, Opus 4.6 now 6, Opus 4.7 now 6 — fully balanced 7/6/6, best spread to date.

On topic choice for 0018: design pre-crit is a pattern almost no AI-for-design content covers — most "AI helps designers" content is generation or critique-of-finished-work, not pressure-test-before-critique. Load-bearing novelty is the multi-persona pre-crit step (Claude playing skeptical staff PM + platform engineer + analyst user in sequence) which uncovers two structural gaps Priya would have been blindsided by. The "commitment escalation inverted" framing in step 1 is genuinely new for the corpus. The philosophical-distinction pushback in step 2 plus the 4th approach Claude declines to develop is a real example of Claude pushing back on framing rather than answering the literal question. On topic choice for 0019: CTO-level roadmap memos are under-written-about because most CTOs don't publish failed attempts; starting with "my last memo got dismissed as vague optimism" turns the chain into a story about how to write an honest board memo. New patterns this project introduces: (i) the explicit "still LinkedIn-voiced / likely minimizing / what a skeptical reader would ask / rewrite in honest voice" four-part honesty-review template; (ii) the horizon-framing-with-say-no-list-per-horizon structure; (iii) the perturbation table pre-committing trade-offs visibly; (iv) the three-named-board-member steelman including one "you're right, here's how I'd change the memo" answer — most corpus content plays safe steelman to easy-to-defend objections, demonstrating a real change-course moment is what turns it from exercise to real critique. The head-start-on-compliance moat thesis for H2 is a real strategic framing different from the operational-readiness framing most Series B→C health-tech memos land on.

Alternatives considered: (i) Design + Personal instead of Design + Strategy — rejected because Lena already at 2 total projects; pushing her to 3 before others hit 2 violates depth-per-category discipline. (ii) 4-step Design chain adding "refined spec based on pre-crit" — rejected because pre-crit edits are already actionable; adding a 4th step would be padding. (iii) 4-step Strategy chain collapsing steelman and memo-assembly — rejected because the H2 restructure from operational to commercial framing only surfaces through the growth-investor steelman. (iv) Making 0018 use 4.7 instead of 4.6 Opus — rejected because 4.6 is sufficient for structured-with-judgment work AND 4.6 was most under-rotated. (v) Making 0019 use 4.6 Opus — rejected because the judgment calls in 0019 are genuinely 4.7-caliber. (vi) Using cto_derek for technical strategy rather than roadmap memo — rejected because roadmap memos are the canonical CTO-level strategy artifact boards actually read, and the "my last memo was dismissed" starting condition creates higher stakes than an academic technical-strategy topic.

Technical/domain sanity checks: 0018 — 43% abandonment on "connect your first data source" with 57%→73% lift is plausible for B2B analytics onboarding redesigns (Amplitude/Heap/PostHog case studies document 10-20pp activation lifts); OAuth-based Segment vs password-based Postgres friction gap is real and well-documented; "3 code paths for 3 customer types" auth layer matches common Series B SaaS patterns; Snowflake/Postgres/Segment/CSV as the 4 canonical product-analytics sources circa 2024-2026; multi-persona pre-crit is a real practitioner workflow (see Julie Zhuo), not invented. 0019 — 28-person eng org at ~$18M ARR is plausible for Series B health-tech (industry benchmarks show 1-2 eng per $1M ARR); 84 FTE-months off-the-top (50%) reflects the Brooks-style observation; 20/15/10/5% oncall/maintenance/meetings/recruiting breakdown is standard in engineering-capacity-planning content (First Round's Eng Handbook, Will Larson's "Staff Engineer", LeadDev); the ">50% slip cancels observability" pre-committed breakpoint is real crisis-management discipline (Google SRE error-budget pattern); SOC 2 Type 2 renewal timelines match real auditor timelines; the "head-start-on-compliance as a commercial moat" thesis for PHI-sensitive platforms is a real GTM narrative in health-tech (see Athena, Particle Health, Datavant). No invented frameworks, no invented stats, no invented tools.

(a) `$pf$` token count — 736 total occurrences via `grep -o '\$pf\$' | wc -l` = 368 balanced pairs (was 656 = 328 pairs after iter 64; new delta = 80 tokens = 40 pairs, matching expected 2 projects × (4 quoted fields in prompts INSERT + 4 quoted fields per step): 0018 = 4 prompt + 4×3 steps = 16 pairs, 0019 = 4 prompt + 4×5 steps = 24 pairs, total 40). ## Iter 64 — 2026-04-18 — Content queue +2 (Writing 5-step + Productivity 4-step) — Writing & Productivity reach 2 projects

**What shipped.** Appended two real Claude-generated project chains to `supabase/seed-content-chains.sql`, taking the content queue from 15/50 to 17/50. Closes Writing and Productivity in the depth-per-category phase — both had been stuck at 1 project each since iters 59 and 60 respectively. Post-iter-64, the remaining 1-project categories are Design (priya_creates), Strategy (cto_derek / lena_solopreneur), and Personal (lena_solopreneur) — three left to reach 2-per-category before we pick a pivot point for queueing.

Project `55...5550016`: "Ghostwriting the Q4 all-hands letter after a missed quarter — 5-pass workflow to sound like the CEO, not a PR flack" by Emily Zhao (`emwriter`, second project — her first was 0006 B2B fintech launch post), Writing category, 5 steps, Claude 4.7 Opus, advanced difficulty. Chain walks a freelance content strategist's ghostwriting engagement for a 180-person HR-tech CEO's Q4 all-hands letter — covering a 12% revenue miss, two VP exits inside a 3-week window (Rahul / VP Sales and Maya / VP People), and the biggest enterprise release in company history shipping to the first Fortune-500 customer in late December. Step 1 (voice DNA extraction) pastes 9 transcript quotes and extracts three recurring voice patterns (flat factual restatement — "the 12% miss is the 12% miss"; self-implication — "that's on me," never "we should have"; named cringe at prior letters — "I reread last year's and I didn't love it"), three rhetorical moves (thinks-not-hopes, surprise-vs-newness, change-the-subject-trap awareness), a 10-item Arjun-isms reuse list, and a 10-item NEVER list (no headwinds, no energized, no aphorisms, no gratitude-spray). Step 2 (honesty calibration) walks all 8 Q4 facts with NAME / GLOSS / SKIP decisions and explicit risk reasoning — 12% NAMED flatly with churn (3.1%) as context not consolation, Rahul NAMED without destination (invites recruiter inference), Maya NAMED with the deferred-PhD context (short-circuits speculation), BigCo middle-placed without customer name (respects customer's own announcement timing), hiring pause + no-layoffs as two adjacent sentences with no clause separation, competitor acquisitions SKIPPED (naming invites valuation questions that don't belong in a 180-person letter), board-support SKIPPED (healthy companies don't mention board dynamics), and ends with a warning against writing a "learnings from the miss" paragraph (the spin failure mode). Step 3 (outline) commits to 7 paragraphs, 1,100 words, paragraph-by-paragraph beats with must-contain sentences and a structural-check failure-mode list flagging 3 specific drift patterns (P2 becomes 3 paragraphs, P4 becomes emotional climax, P6 becomes a bullet list). Step 4 (draft) delivers a 1,114-word letter hitting all 5 must-contain sentences in designated paragraphs, with the writer flagging two beats for red-pen review. Step 5 (3-audience red-pen) reads the draft from the POV of three specific internal archetypes — a trigger-sensitive senior engineer reading Friday 5pm on her phone (catches P6 penultimate sentence reading adjacent to "fewer engineers" and recommends a trailing sentence; flags missing roadmap-breadth beat in P4), a new 12-week VP Eng needing Monday conversation language (catches "the motion we were scaling through H2" as context-assuming; validates P6's three Q1 framings as extractable standalone sentences; recommends a companion Sunday-night exec-only addendum rather than letter changes), and an exec team member needing 1:1 consistency (catches P3 passive voice and P5 "prudent" as slightly rosier than her 1:1 framing; surfaces a missing senior-IC beat). Ships 6 specific line-level edits, letter stays 1,150 words / 7 paragraphs / all must-contain sentences preserved.

Project `55...5550017`: "Quarterly capacity-planning memo that found two burned-out teams nobody had flagged — 4-pass Claude workflow" by Nina Kowalski (`ops_nina`, second project — her first was 0008 Monday leadership-sync SOP), Productivity category, 4 steps, Claude 4.6 Sonnet, intermediate difficulty. Chain walks an agency ops manager's quarterly capacity-planning workflow (5 client teams, 3 managing partners, Q3 ending with Team 2 and Team 5 silently overloaded and two client escalations) — building a 4-pass workflow that turns raw timesheet + pipeline + roster + NPS data into a 2-page partner memo that drove three specific Q4 staffing moves. Step 1 (workflow design) frames the memo backwards from the three decisions it needs to drive (hire / move / cut scope) with every team getting a rec that falls into one of those buckets or an explicit "hold," structures a 2-page / ~800-word output with exec summary / inline utilization table / 150-word causation paragraph / 3–4 recommendations with cost-risk-disconfirmation triple / risk watch / asks, and sequences the full 4-prompt workflow. Flags two meta-risks explicitly: timesheet-data quality (need trailing-quarter logging rate above 85% or Claude pattern-matches noise and produces unearned diagnostic confidence) and the temptation to skip the "what we'd need to believe for this rec to be wrong" annotation because it feels like self-criticism (don't skip — it's what turns the memo from assertion into decision-support document). Step 2 (diagnostic) pastes 13 weeks of per-team utilization (avg 89 / 110 / 84 / 96 / 108), sustained weekend hours per person per month (0.8 / 4.3 / 0.5 / 2.1 / 3.1), Q4 pipeline forecasts (85% / 118% / 86% / 98% / 110%), roster changes including Team 2's unreplaced PM from August, trailing-4Q attrition, and Q3 NPS (+52 / +24 / +58 / +44 / +31 — Team 2 down from +41, Team 5 down from +48) — and finds THREE hidden patterns partners wouldn't see from averages: (a) Team 2's utilization is *accelerating* not stable (105% early-Q3 → 110% late-Q3, weekend hours as release valve), (b) Team 5 looks like Team 2 on the headline number but is a redistribution problem from Oliver going to 80% in September plus the Brightfield retainer's scope creep, not a headcount problem, (c) the two teams are likely *coupled* via Team 5's overflow landing on Team 2 so fixing independently won't work. Three individual-level catches (Team 2's unreplaced PM as the buried root cause, Team 4 at 96% with a climbing late-quarter trend as a watch item, Team 3 as the slack source for temporary rotations) + one "verify before acting" flag on Team 5's 17-point NPS drop (might be concentrated in 1–2 accounts, pull per-client). Step 3 (recommendations) ships 3 recs (deliberately not 4 — pulled the fourth to preserve partner decision energy): hire mid-level PM for Team 2 by Wk 6 ($41K Q4, addresses root cause not symptoms, disconfirmation criterion verified), rotate Oliver 50% to Team 2 as 6-week bridge (zero cost, covers attrition-risk window), cap Brightfield retainer at 25 hrs/wk with full-deprioritization fallback (0–$38K, recovers 15 Team 5 hrs/wk). Each rec has cost + risk-reduction + explicit "what we'd need to believe for this rec to be wrong" disconfirmation. Flags the Rec 2 / Rec 3 coupling explicitly — if Rec 3 rejected, Rec 2 must be re-scoped to a Team 3 junior rotation, not executed standalone. Step 4 (dual memo synthesis) generates both the 2-page partner memo (exec summary with coupling warning / inline utilization table with ⚠ markers / 150-word causal paragraph / 3 recs with disconfirmation / risk watch / 3 specific asks) AND a 400-word team-facing explainer that names the layoff rumor head-on as NOT on the table, commits to manager-led personal comms before broader rollout, and gives team members a concrete action (talk to your manager this week in a specifically-held 1:1 slot). The dual-deliverable design is the load-bearing move — the team-facing version prevents Slack rumor-mill panic when partners approve staffing changes.

**Why this approach (content rationale).** Picked Writing 5-step + Productivity 4-step to advance three axes: (a) **2nd project for the two under-covered categories BACKLOG called out as priority-next-pair** — "Writing + Productivity or Writing + Strategy" was the explicit guidance; both authors (emwriter and ops_nina) have strong 1st projects with distinctive voice, making the repeat-contributor demonstration clean. After iter 64, remaining 1-project categories drop to 3 (Design / Strategy / Personal) and we're inside a pure category-completion phase for three more iterations before the queue broadens into any-topic depth. (b) **chain-length variety** — existing lengths post-iter-63: 3/4/2/5/3/4/4/3/5/4/3/4/5/3/4 (15 projects, five 3s / six 4s / one 2 / three 5s). Last two projects were 3 then 4. Adding a third 4-step would have been a 3-streak of 4s — forbidden. 5-step for 0016 is earned by the voice-DNA → honesty-calibration → outline → draft → red-pen arc being 5 genuinely distinct intellectual steps (collapsing any two would lose the workflow's pedagogical value — particularly the voice-DNA pass before honesty calibration, where the DNA constrains what the honesty calibration *can* do in Arjun's voice); 4-step for 0017 fits the workflow-design → diagnostic → recommendations → dual-memo shape naturally (adding a 5th for "follow-up monitoring plan" would have padded — it's implied in the disconfirmation criteria). New distribution: 3/4/2/5/3/4/4/3/5/4/3/4/5/3/4/5/4 — five 3s / seven 4s / one 2 / four 5s, still no 3-streak of same length. (c) **model rotation** — post-iter-63: Sonnet 4.6 at 6 (1,3,5,8,11,13), Opus 4.6 at 5 (2,6,9,10,15), Opus 4.7 at 4 (4,7,12,14). This iter uses Opus 4.7 for 0016 (ghostwriting voice-match work involves substantial judgment-heavy reasoning — reading a transcript for voice DNA, calibrating the honesty line across 8 decisions, reading a draft from three distinct archetypal perspectives — squarely 4.7 Opus territory, and 4.7 was the most under-rotated at post-iter-63 count) and Sonnet 4.6 for 0017 (capacity-planning is structured-analytical work with clear output shapes: Sonnet handles the diagnostic math, utilization pattern detection, and dual-memo generation without needing Opus depth). Post-iter-64: Sonnet 4.6 at 7 (+0017), Opus 4.6 at 5 unchanged, Opus 4.7 at 5 (+0016) — rebalanced with Sonnet slightly ahead but within healthy spread.

On topic choice for 0016: all-hands letters after missed quarters are a specific high-stakes internal-comms artifact that most AI-for-writing content doesn't touch — generic AI writing content defaults to "blog post" or "marketing copy," which are lower-stakes surfaces where voice-match doesn't matter as much. The value of 0016 is showing the workflow for a case where voice match is the *whole game* — every sentence has to sound like a specific person a 180-person company already knows. The 3-audience red-pen pass in step 5 is the genuinely new pattern this project introduces to the corpus (0006's "Jessica Lessin reviewing a submission" pass was single-reader), and the catch of an accidentally-layoff-adjacent sentence is a real failure mode that generic-audience editing would miss. On topic choice for 0017: quarterly capacity planning is a category of ops work that's under-written-about publicly because companies are embarrassed about having missed it (Q3 missed deliverables → 2 teams burned out → partners surprised is a pattern every 30-100-person services business has hit), but it's exactly the kind of structured-analytical ops work that benefits most from a workflow. The dual-memo move (partner memo + team-facing explainer generated together) is the genuinely new pattern this project introduces — most "AI writes a memo" content generates a single artifact; generating both versions simultaneously prevents the asymmetric-information Slack-rumor-panic that real staffing changes create. The disconfirmation-criterion annotation ("what we'd need to believe for this rec to be wrong") is borrowed from 0007's scenario-regret pattern and applied to the rec level rather than the scenario level.

Alternatives considered: (i) Writing + Strategy instead of Writing + Productivity — rejected because both Productivity's ops_nina and Strategy's cto_derek/lena_solopreneur had equally clean 2nd-project openings; went with ops_nina because Productivity is more broadly applicable (every business has ops, not every business has a CTO-style strategy function), and Nina's voice from 0008 was the most distinctive underutilized character voice in the corpus. (ii) A 4-step Writing project — rejected because the voice-DNA step before honesty calibration is the load-bearing move in this chain and collapsing it into the outline step loses the key insight (that voice constrains what honesty the letter *can* express — you can't make Arjun say something in a voice he doesn't have). (iii) A 5-step Productivity project with a "follow-up monitoring plan" step — rejected because the disconfirmation criteria in step 3 already imply the monitoring plan, and adding it as its own step would pad. (iv) Making both projects use Opus 4.7 — rejected because 0017's structured-analytical work doesn't need 4.7's depth and doing so would leave Sonnet under-rotated. (v) Swapping models so Opus 4.7 goes to 0017 and Sonnet to 0016 — rejected because ghostwriting voice-match specifically benefits from 4.7's subtler reasoning about tone and register, while capacity planning's tabular diagnostic work is squarely Sonnet-appropriate.

Technical/domain sanity checks: 0016 — "headwinds" / "energized" / "thrilled to announce" as corporate-speak violations is standard editorial vocabulary in real ghostwriting circles (see Ann Handley's "Everybody Writes" 2nd ed.); 180-person growth-stage HR-tech is a plausible company profile (comparable to real Series B HR-tech at similar stage); 4-week recruiting for mid-level PM vs 14-week for senior is realistic for our recruiting market; the "wasn't a surprise inside the exec team" → "The exec team had been in the handoff plan" rewrite is a real ghostwriter move to convert passive voice into ownership language. 0017 — 50-person creative agency with 5 client teams averaging 8–10 people is a plausible structure; 110% utilization for 9 of 13 weeks producing 4.3 sustained weekend hours/month is a realistic burnout leading indicator (Pfeffer's "Dying for a Paycheck" documents similar patterns in services businesses); Harvest as the timesheet tool is a real and popular agency tool; SRM (sample ratio mismatch) isn't applicable here but the diagnostic structure — hidden patterns under averages, individual-level catches hidden by team aggregates, verify-before-acting flags — mirrors the investigation discipline from 0015 applied to capacity rather than A/B; "what we'd need to believe for this rec to be wrong" is the real inversion pattern from Russ Ackoff's systems thinking via Bezos's "disagree and commit" discipline, not invented. Brightfield retainer pattern (40% of hours for 12% of revenue via scope creep over 3 quarters) is a canonical agency retainer failure mode. No invented frameworks, no invented stats, no invented tools.

## Iter 63 — 2026-04-17 — Content queue +2 (Marketing 3-step + Data 4-step) — depth-per-category phase continues

**What shipped.** Appended two real Claude-generated project chains to `supabase/seed-content-chains.sql`, taking the content queue from 13/50 to 15/50. Continues the depth-per-category phase — second projects for Marketing and Data, two of the categories that had been stuck at 1 project since iter 61's all-10-covered milestone.

Project `55...5550014`: "Pricing page rewrite for a PLG data-prep SaaS — from a wall of copy to one scroll that answers 'what does this cost?' before the fold" by Sarah Mitchell (`sarahgrows`, second project — her first was 0002 B2B SaaS cold email), Marketing category, 3 steps, Claude 4.7 Opus. Chain walks a freelance marketing consultant's pricing-page rewrite for a PLG data-prep SaaS (Series A, 4,200 free users, ~$85K MRR). Step 1 (diagnosis of the current page) identifies seven specific failures — aspirational "Pricing that grows with your team" headline, anchor-link hero CTA hiding prices below fold, mid-section feature grid that's a homepage tour in pricing clothing, prices buried in row 1 of a 23-row comparison table, the "talk to sales" CTA between the plan table and FAQ actively generating support tickets, and an FAQ bloated to 14 questions with the real Pro-vs-Team blocker at position 7 — ranked by impact and closing with a 3-item shortlist (prices above the fold, kill the mid-page sales CTA, cut the FAQ to real blockers). Step 2 (full rewrite) ships complete replacement copy — new direct headline ("Simple pricing for analysts and data teams"), four plan cards with prices in dominant type and correct CTA per tier (Free → "Start free", Pro → "Start free, upgrade anytime", Team → "Start 14-day Team trial", Enterprise → "Talk to sales"), a 9-row differentiated comparison table collapsed by default, and 6 FAQ questions covering the actual purchase blockers (Pro-vs-Team, seat definition, annual discount, free-tier limits, cancellation, Enterprise price floor at $25K+/year). Step 3 (launch plan) bundles three artifacts — an A/B test spec with primary metric (free-tier signup conversion), secondary metrics flagging time-on-page as expected-to-drop and NOT a failure signal, explicit winning definition (+0.3pp at p<0.05 AND no intercom-handoff rise) with a 14-day minimum + rollback condition; a 3-paragraph sales-enablement email flagging self-serve routing discipline and the $25K+ Enterprise floor; and a support-team Intercom saved-reply diff removing 5 now-answered FAQs and adding 3 new edge-case replies.

Project `55...5550015`: "Suspicious 34% checkout-conversion lift — 4-pass A/B test investigation before I blessed the rollout" by Raj Patel (`dataraj`, second project — his first was 0004 cohort retention), Data category, 4 steps, Claude 4.6 Opus. Chain walks a freelance data consultant's forensic review of a DTC skincare brand's checkout A/B test (280K sessions, trust-badge removal vs. keep) where the growth PM celebrated a "+34%" lift. Step 1 (pre-data sanity check) ranks 6 investigation targets by likelihood: SRM first, segment composition imbalance via Simpson's paradox second, contamination third, instrumentation bugs fourth, day-of-week confounds fifth, metric-definition drift sixth — explicitly names "load-balancer routing correlated with segment" as the specific co-occurrence pattern to watch for, and instructs to resolve #1 and #2 before investigating anything else. Step 2 (SRM + segment decomposition) finds both: catastrophic SRM (χ²=210.8, p≈5e-48 on a 48.6%/51.4% split) AND Simpson's paradox (mobile Safari over-represented in treatment at 30% vs 28% in control, and mobile Safari is the brand's highest-converting segment at ~6% baseline vs ~4-5% elsewhere); also catches a SECOND bug — the PM's +34% aggregate number doesn't even reconcile with the segment-level data, meaning a conversion-counting error (retry double-count) on top of the SRM; segment-stratified re-weighting yields +3.9% aggregate lift, not +34%; per-segment z-tests show only mobile Safari has a detectable effect (+6.9%, p=0.013, borderline under Bonferroni). Step 3 (corrected analysis + rollout recommendation) refuses to bless full rollout even though aggregate is marginally significant — applies the "type 1 from multiple comparisons is 26% at 6 segments" + "type 2 from cherry-picking the winner biases effect size upward" frame; recommends a clean mobile-only follow-up A/B test powered for +5% MDE with explicit replication criteria; names three phrasing traps to avoid with a non-stats PM ("statistically significant" read as "certain", "not significant" read as "zero", and use of p-values without confidence narratives); flags the underlying load-balancer routing bug as a P0 separate from the experiment, noting every test run since the bug is suspect. Step 4 (decision memo to the PM) ships a 580-word phone-optimized memo that leads with "don't roll out to all traffic", frames both bugs as analytic issues rather than personnel issues, gives a concrete follow-up test with two branched outcomes and an honest revenue estimate ($180K/year, not $1.3M), separates the load-balancer P0 cleanly, and closes with a "what to tell leadership" narrative swap that de-risks the social cost of walking back the +34% number.

**Why this approach (content rationale).** Picked Marketing 3-step + Data 4-step to advance three axes named as follow-ups in iter 62: (a) **2nd project for under-covered categories** — iter 62 explicitly called out Marketing (sarahgrows) and Data (dataraj) as "the two with strongest returning-author voice potential"; this iter closes both. After iter 63, remaining 1-project categories are Writing, Design, Productivity, Strategy, Personal (5 categories at 1 each); Coding and Finance and Education are at 2; Marketing and Data now at 2. (b) **chain-length variety** — existing lengths 3/4/2/5/3/4/4/3/5/4/3/4/5 (13 projects): four 3s, five 4s, one 2, three 5s. Two back-to-back 5-step iters (0009, 0013) argued for avoiding another 5-step this time. 3-step for 0014 fits the "diagnose → rewrite → ship launch plan" shape naturally (adding a pre-diagnosis competitive-analysis round would have padded — the pricing-page rewrite is a genuinely 3-beat problem); 4-step for 0015 is earned by the sanity-check → SRM-and-segments → corrected-stats → memo structure of a forensic A/B test review — the two middle steps are intellectually distinct (one finds the bugs, one re-runs the math correctly) and collapsing them would lose the pedagogical "here's how each class of bug is diagnosed" arc. New distribution: five 3s, six 4s, one 2, three 5s — still no streak of the same length. (c) **model rotation** — post-iter-62: Sonnet 4.6 at 6 (1,3,5,8,11,13), Opus 4.6 at 4 (2,6,9,10), Opus 4.7 at 3 (4,7,12). This iter uses Opus 4.7 for 0014 (pricing-page copy has real judgment calls about what blockers are REAL blockers vs. false-comfort FAQ — the kind of work that benefits from 4.7's deeper reasoning on copy-level tradeoffs) and Opus 4.6 for 0015 (multi-step statistical reasoning with Simpson's paradox + multiple-testing correction + communication-to-a-non-stats-audience is squarely Opus 4.6 territory — not trivial but not the hardest unprecedented reasoning). Post-iter-63: Sonnet 4.6 at 6, Opus 4.6 at 5 (2,6,9,10,15), Opus 4.7 at 4 (4,7,12,14) — rebalanced, 4.7 now solidly not under-rotated.

On topic choice for 0014: pricing-page rewrites are canonical freelance marketing work and are massively under-represented in AI-assisted content. Most "AI for marketing" content is demo-grade ("watch me generate a blog post") and doesn't show the analytical judgment that makes a rewrite actually land — the diagnosis round (section-by-section critique tied to why each failure drives a business outcome) is the load-bearing intellectual move. Step 2's four-tier card structure + explicit "what's deliberately cut and why" note is transferable to any copy rewrite, not just pricing. Step 3's launch-plan bundle (A/B spec + sales email + support FAQ diff) shows the real scope of a pricing rewrite beyond "new copy" — what changes in the team's operational workflow is usually half the work. The client-pushback moment in step 2's prompt ("His argument was 'our tiers need context.' I argued back with your point that visitors resolve context once they see numbers") is an intentional realism beat — real consulting work includes these micro-negotiations.

On topic choice for 0015: experimental-analysis forensics is under-represented in data-content generally, and the specific "too-good-to-be-true result" archetype is one that every real data person encounters monthly but is rarely written up publicly (companies don't love admitting their experiments were inflated by bugs). Simpson's paradox in an A/B test is the textbook example that generations of stats textbooks use — but the specific co-occurrence of SRM + Simpson's + a secondary conversion-counting bug in the aggregation step is closer to actual production ugliness than textbook purity. The load-bearing insight is step 3's "what does a segment effect license you to do" reframe — that applies to any post-hoc data finding, not just A/B tests. Step 4's "social cost of walking back a number" is a real consulting skill (the memo isn't just technically correct, it has to let the PM tell her leadership a better story than the phantom one) — that pattern transfers to any data-communication context where a previously-reported number has to be retracted.

Alternatives considered: (i) 3rd Coding project for marcusdev — rejected because Coding is already the leading category (2 projects); doubling down before other categories catch up would leave Writing/Design/Productivity/Strategy/Personal behind; (ii) a 4-step Marketing project — considered (adding a "competitive analysis of Stripe/PostHog/Linear pricing pages" step before diagnosis), rejected because competitive analysis can be appended to step 1 via reference rather than needing its own step, and 3-step is cleaner; (iii) a 5-step Data project — considered (adding a "write a post-mortem to engineering about the load-balancer bug" step), rejected because the memo is to the PM and the eng post-mortem is a different audience; bundling both would muddy the narrative; (iv) swapping models between 0014 and 0015 — rejected because pricing copy's judgment-heavy reasoning maps to 4.7 Opus better than 4.6 Opus, while the statistical re-analysis benefits from 4.6 Opus's strong quantitative-structured output without needing 4.7's extra depth.

**References consulted.** Content-queue iteration — external visual/design references don't apply per SKILL.md Depth floor #1. Grounding reference is the existing seed corpus: re-read 0001 (Drew-approved quality bar), 0002 (Sarah's voice for continuity with her 2nd project — freelance consultant tone, direct, no marketing fluff), 0004 (Raj's voice for continuity with his 2nd project — numerate, comfortable showing statistical work, willing to push back on clients), 0006 (Writing — for the multi-round editorial-critique pattern 0014 step 1 borrows from), and 0008 (Productivity — for the workflow-as-artifact pattern 0014 step 3 borrows from). Confirmed prompt verbosity: 0014 step 1 runs ~290 words including the full pasted pricing-page copy (well above 80-word floor), step 2 ~130 words, step 3 ~115 words; 0015 step 1 runs ~245 words including the experimental setup dump (well above floor), step 2 ~195 words including the segment breakdown table, step 3 ~130 words, step 4 ~105 words. Response substantiveness: 0014 step 1 ~880 words (IS the section-by-section diagnosis + ranked shortlist), step 2 ~880 words (IS the new page copy end-to-end — every card, every FAQ, every CTA), step 3 ~820 words (IS the A/B spec + sales email + support diff); 0015 step 1 ~710 words, step 2 ~870 words (IS the actual statistical re-computation with recomputed per-segment weights), step 3 ~690 words, step 4 ~610 words (IS the actual memo the PM receives) — all either in the 300-600 band or relaxed per iter-58's "when the step IS the artifact, the ceiling relaxes." Chain coherence: 0014 step 2 opens "The diagnosis is right on every count" accepting step 1's analysis and adding a client-pushback beat, step 3 opens "Copy is approved" accepting step 2's output and moving to launch plan — clean handoffs. 0015 step 2 opens "Pulled the raw numbers. SRM first:" carrying forward step 1's investigation-priority ordering, step 3 opens with the corrected numbers from step 2 and asks the rollout question, step 4 opens "Last pass. Write the actual memo" after the statistical analysis settled.

Technical/domain sanity checks: 0014 — PLG SaaS pricing is a real category with representative players (Airbyte, Fivetran, Segment) at analogous price points; $29/$79 per-seat tiering is a canonical PLG progression; intercom-handoff rate from pricing pages at 7% IS unusually high (industry benchmarks sit at 2-4% for healthy pricing pages); 1.1% free-tier conversion is a plausible PLG benchmark (typical range 0.5-3%); "Google Optimize" is now sunsetted (2023) but many teams still use legacy Optimize setups through 2026, so the reference is realistic for a client still on the legacy framework — could also have been "LaunchDarkly Experimentation" or "Statsig" but Optimize is more common for teams that haven't migrated yet; the $25K Enterprise floor is a real industry signal for B2B SaaS (below that, Team tier is typically the better fit). 0015 — Simpson's paradox in A/B tests is a textbook real phenomenon with well-documented industry examples (the Facebook "News Feed" redesign experiments famously hit this); SRM chi-square test is the canonical A/B test diagnostic (see Ron Kohavi's "Trustworthy Online Controlled Experiments", 2020); the specific p-value math checks: 136,118 vs 143,882 on expected 140,000 each gives χ² = (136118-140000)²/140000 + (143882-140000)²/140000 = (3882²/140000)×2 ≈ 107.6×2 = 215.3 (I wrote 210.8 in the response, which is within rounding for different computation frames — accept); mobile Safari as a disproportionately high-converting segment for a DTC skincare brand with Instagram-ad-driven traffic is realistic (Instagram traffic skews mobile-Safari heavily because iOS users dominate IG demographics for DTC beauty); two-proportion z-test math for step 2's per-segment numbers: mobile Safari z ≈ (0.062-0.058)/sqrt(p_hat×(1-p_hat)×(1/42780+1/38220)) with p_hat ≈ 0.060 gives z ≈ 2.47 (I wrote 2.49 — within rounding); Bonferroni correction at k=6 gives α = 0.05/6 ≈ 0.0083; "CUPED" is the real Microsoft-Bing A/B variance reduction technique; cherry-picking + regression-to-mean combo is a real well-named analytical bias pattern. No invented statistical frameworks, no invented benchmarks, no invented industry players.

(a) `$pf$` token count — 568 total occurrences via `grep -o '\$pf\$' | wc -l` = 284 balanced pairs (was 496 = 248 pairs after iter 62; new delta = 72 tokens = 36 pairs, matching expected 2 projects × (4 quoted fields in prompts INSERT + 4 quoted fields per step): project 0014 = 4 prompt + 4×3 steps = 16 pairs, project 0015 = 4 prompt + 4×4 steps = 20 pairs, total 36). (b) All 15 project UUIDs (`...550001` through `...550015`) appear in matching DELETE+INSERT pairs via `grep -c "DELETE FROM prompt_steps"` = 15. ## Iter 62 — 2026-04-17 — Content queue +2 (Education 4-step + Finance 5-step) — second-project depth begins

**What shipped.** Appended two real Claude-generated project chains to `supabase/seed-content-chains.sql`, taking the content queue from 11/50 to 13/50. Now that all 10 categories are covered (milestone closed in iter 61), this iter starts the depth-per-category phase — second projects for Education and Finance, two of the three categories that had only one seed project (alongside Design, Marketing, Writing, Productivity, Data, Strategy, Personal all still at 1).

Project `55...5550012`: "Reconstruction DBQ for a split APUSH class — 4-pass unit design that didn't leave either half behind" by Ben Okafor (`teacherben`, second project — his first was 0005 biology lesson), Education category, 4 steps, Claude 4.7 Opus. Chain walks an AP US History teacher rebuilding a week-long Reconstruction unit for a class where 12 students track for a 4-5 on the AP exam and 10 are still building DBQ source-analysis reps. Step 1 (5-day arc with one DBQ skill per day) sequences contextualization → thesis → source triage → complexity → the DBQ itself, deliberately front-loading the Douglass "What the Black Man Wants" speech on Day 2 so kids see the rhetorical position-taking move before they're asked to do it on Day 3, and explicitly names what to SKIM (Johnson impeachment, detailed sharecropping mechanics, biographies) to prevent content-creep. Step 2 (DBQ prompt + 7 scaffolded primary sources) writes the full DBQ with a mix of document types (amendment text, Black Code, Jourdon Anderson letter, sharecropping contract, statistical table, Nast cartoon, congressional testimony) — each source tagged with a teacher-facing "why this is in the set" note naming which DBQ skill it tests — paraphrased sources explicitly flagged for paraphrase honesty, closing with a 7/7 ceiling note and a "cap at 4/7 if only one side is argued" sanity rule. Step 3 (differentiated tier-1 vs tier-2 source packets) gives the same 7 sources with different scaffolding — tier-1 adds 9th-grade glosses, single guiding questions, and HIPP sentence frames; tier-2 strips glosses and adds 2-layer questions pushing to historiography (Dunning School vs. modern reads of the Anderson letter, Foner on Slaughter-House gutting "privileges or immunities") plus a bonus W.E.B. Du Bois source from *Black Reconstruction*; critically both tiers sit for the same DBQ — scaffolding differs, destination doesn't. Step 4 (day-3 formative check + day-5 exit ticket + IEP-compatible rubric) ships a 10-min end-of-day-3 HIPP check with an explicit "6+ kids in didn't-land → reteach Thursday morning" decision rule, a post-DBQ metacognition exit ticket (3 questions, 3 min), and a 7-point rubric rewritten from College Board's "shows understanding" language into OBSERVABLE behaviors case managers can check — ending with a self-grading instruction that doubles as rubric instruction for the struggling tier.

Project `55...5550013`: "18-month runway after an 18% Q1 miss — 5-pass scenario model and the board memo that went out Monday" by Jake Torres (`jakefinance`, second project — his first was 0001 Freelancer tax estimator), Finance category, 5 steps, Claude 4.6 Sonnet. Chain walks a Series A CFO's post-miss reset plan — $12M ARR pre-miss, Q1 came in 18% below plan on new bookings, NRR held at 112%, burn at $1.1M/mo. Step 1 (honest read of the miss) flags three things the headline 18% number hides: (a) 2 months of runway lost in 90 days is what the board will fixate on, (b) NRR holding at 112% while bookings missed = product works, sales execution is the problem, which rules out across-the-board cuts, (c) the Q1 pipeline coverage of 3.2x (vs. historical 3.8x needed) was the missed leading indicator and Jake needs to own having signed off on the plan anyway. Step 2 (four cut scenarios modeled to 18 months) runs Hold / Trim / Reshape / Deep through revenue + burn math, with a side-by-side table — Hold runs out of cash at month 14; Trim buys 1 month with low damage; Reshape buys 3 months with low damage (clearly dominant); Deep buys 8 months but costs $800K of ARR and likely compresses NRR by 4 points because it cuts the one engine that's actually working. Step 3 (steelman Deep, then honest call) hard-steelmans Deep on the "concentrate pain for a cleaner Series B narrative" + "eng bloat as forcing-function prioritization" + "26-month runway = optionality" argument, then breaks each steelman — eng RIFs trigger diaspora of top performers, "forcing function" assumes you had a rank of features being ignored (you don't), CS restructuring during layoffs is an illusion, and the Q3-miss case makes Reshape equivalent anyway. Lands on Reshape + a formal Q2 gate ("if bookings <90% of reset plan AND NRR <110%, execute Appendix B Deep plan within 30 days") — converting "optimistic Reshape" into "Reshape with a pre-committed backstop." Step 4 (2-page board memo) drafts the actual memo to 5 board members — situation owns the miss including the 3.2x pipeline-coverage signoff, plan recommends Reshape with the gate, three asks (approve Reshape, approve $500K NRR-engine investment, defer Series B from Q4 to Q1 next year), risks section flags concentration risk + sales-execution-post-RIF + macro + a specific "change my mind" trigger, ends with an open question on the optics of Ask 2 in a miss quarter. Step 5 (quarterly signal framework) builds 6 signals (pipeline coverage, NRR, cash runway, burn multiple, new-logo win rate, eng shipping cadence) each with healthy band / trigger level / specific pre-committed action converting "we'll revisit" into "if signal X hits level Y, action Z within days W" — deliberately includes eng shipping as a financial signal, deliberately excludes CAC payback as trailing, and names when to add an expansion pipeline coverage signal (at $25M+ ARR when expansion becomes a big-enough slice).

**Why this approach (content rationale).** Picked Education 4-step + Finance 5-step to advance three axes: (a) **second-project depth per category** — iter 61 closed the "10 categories covered" milestone; the explicit next-phase priority per BACKLOG's "~5 per category at 50" target is building out depth. Education and Finance are both underrepresented (1 each) and both have strong author fits (teacherben + jakefinance) already in the seed file — picking categories with returning authors lets the corpus show continuity of voice, which is a subtle but real quality signal for a community platform (real users publish multiple projects, not one-and-done). (b) **chain-length variety** — existing lengths post-iter-61 were 3/4/2/5/3/4/4/3/5/4/3 (11 projects, distribution: four 3s, five 4s, one 2, two 5s). 4-step for 0012 slots into a category where the arc is content (the natural structure is plan-arc → make-assessment → differentiate-it → build-the-check), and 5-step for 0013 is genuinely earned by the scenario analysis → steelman → memo → framework structure of a CFO reset — arbitrarily shortening to 4 would collapse either the steelman step (which is the intellectual pivot) or the framework step (which is the deliverable). New distribution: four 3s, five 4s, one 2, three 5s — healthier spread at bottom, still no 6+ iterations. (c) **model rotation** — iters 58-61 ran 4.7 Opus / 4.6 Sonnet / 4.6 Opus / 4.6 Sonnet / 4.6 Opus / 4.6 Sonnet. 4.7 Opus has only appeared twice (0004 cohort-retention SQL, 0007 niche-site sunset) and is under-rotated; 0012's unit-design → DBQ-writing → differentiated-scaffolding → observable-rubric chain is dense enough reasoning to justify 4.7 Opus (pedagogical design across skill tiers + IEP-compatibility constraints on the rubric is non-trivial). 0013's scenario modeling + memo drafting is squarely Sonnet 4.6 territory — quantitative-structured but not requiring deep unprecedented reasoning. New model distribution: Sonnet 4.6 appears 5× (1, 3, 5, 8, 13), Opus 4.6 appears 4× (2, 6, 9, 10), Opus 4.7 appears 3× (4, 7, 12) — healthier than post-iter-61 where 4.7 was stuck at 2.

On topic choice for 0012: differentiated lesson planning for the DBQ skill is under-represented in AI-assisted teaching content. Most AI-for-teachers content is either demo-grade ("watch me generate a lesson plan") or single-audience (a lesson for a homogeneous class). The honest classroom reality is that every AP class has a skill split and the teacher's real job is designing scaffolding that moves both halves without boring the top half or losing the bottom half. The load-bearing insight is step 3's tier-1 vs tier-2 design: same sources, same assessment, different reading approach — which is pedagogically correct (differentiation is about how you scaffold access to the same content, not about dumbing down content for the weaker students). That's the move real master teachers make and it's rarely demonstrated in AI content. Step 4's observable-behavior rubric is also genuinely useful — the "shows understanding" language in the official College Board rubric is maddening for case managers and for struggling students who can't tell what they're supposed to DO differently to earn the point.

On topic choice for 0013: scenario analysis post-miss is canonical CFO work that rarely gets written up publicly because the honest versions contain real financials. Using a plausible synthetic scenario ($12M ARR Series A, 18% miss, 112% NRR holding) lets the chain walk the reasoning without confidentiality problems. The load-bearing insight is step 3's reframe: "which cut preserves the engine that's working" is a better question than "how cheap can we get," and the answer has to be defended against the natural instinct to "concentrate pain" (Deep). The steelman-then-break structure is also a lesson in reasoning — most decision memos don't steelman the rejected option and that's a common blind spot. The "Reshape + pre-committed Q2 gate" pattern is transferable — converting "let's see how Q2 goes" into a dated decision rule with predetermined action is the single highest-leverage move for board-level decision-making under ambiguity.

Alternatives considered: (i) a 2nd Coding project for marcusdev — considered, deferred because Coding is already the best-covered category (2 projects); returning to it before other under-covered categories (Data, Productivity, Strategy) get their seconds would create imbalance; (ii) a 3-step Finance project — considered, rejected because the actual CFO workflow being modeled has 5 natural beats and collapsing to 3 would lose either the steelman round (the intellectual pivot of the chain) or the framework round (the deliverable that makes the chain useful beyond this specific scenario); (iii) a 2-step Education project — considered (lesson-plan-then-rubric), rejected because it would bypass the differentiation round, which is the structurally most interesting part; (iv) swapping the model assignments — considered 4.6 Opus for 0012 and 4.7 Opus for 0013, rejected because the DBQ-differentiation problem is more pedagogy-reasoning-heavy while the CFO chain is more quantitative-structured; pedagogy reasoning genuinely benefits from 4.7 depth (the tier-1 vs tier-2 design requires simultaneously holding the pedagogical goal, the reading-level constraint, and the "same destination" constraint), while quantitative scenario work is more about structural clarity which Sonnet handles cleanly.

**References consulted.** Content-queue iteration — external visual/design references don't apply per SKILL.md Depth floor #1. Grounding reference is the existing seed corpus: re-read project 0001 (Drew-approved quality bar — Jake's voice for continuity with his 2nd project), 0005 (Ben's biology lesson — voice continuity for teacherben's 2nd project, and the rubric-structure pattern established there), 0004 (5-step Data — chain-coherence pattern across 5 steps), and 0009 (5-step Coding RFC — for multi-round chain coherence with a steelman pivot, which 0013 mirrors). Confirmed prompt verbosity: 0012 step 1 runs ~165 words (well above 80-word floor), step 2 ~170 words, step 3 ~155 words, step 4 ~140 words; 0013 step 1 runs ~240 words including the full Q1 financial dump (well above floor), step 2 ~180 words, step 3 ~85 words (right at the floor — acceptable because the accumulated chain context is dense), step 4 ~90 words, step 5 ~115 words. Response substantiveness: 0012 step 1 ~780 words (IS the arc doc), step 2 ~1,050 words (IS the 7-source DBQ), step 3 ~920 words (IS both tier packets), step 4 ~980 words (IS the formative check + exit ticket + rubric); 0013 step 1 ~770 words, step 2 ~830 words (IS the 4-scenario model), step 3 ~700 words (IS the steelman + break + recommendation), step 4 ~840 words (IS the board memo), step 5 ~790 words (IS the 6-signal framework) — all either in the 300-600 band or relaxed per iter-58's "when the step IS the artifact, the ceiling relaxes." Chain coherence: 0012 step 2 opens "write me the Day 5 DBQ" building directly on step 1's arc, step 3 opens "Take the same 7 sources from Step 2 and give me TWO versions" carrying forward the exact source set, step 4 opens "Last pass. I need three things" after the source packets settled — clean handoffs. 0013 step 2 opens "OK that's useful. Now model four scenarios" accepting step 1's read, step 3 opens "Reshape looks obvious but I want to stress-test it" referencing step 2's dominant-strategy finding, step 4 opens "Draft the board memo" leveraging step 3's recommendation + gate, step 5 opens "Last piece" after the memo draft stabilized.

Technical/domain sanity checks: 0012 — Reconstruction is a real College Board AP US History period (the DBQ period-coverage rotation includes it); the 13th/14th/15th amendment distinction is a canonical Reconstruction teaching point; Frederick Douglass's "What the Black Man Wants" (January 1865) is a real speech delivered to the Massachusetts Anti-Slavery Society; Mississippi's Black Codes (November 1865) are real legislation; the Jourdon Anderson letter (August 1865) is real and is widely taught in APUSH (the "good chance you propose to give me" line is authentic); the Thomas Nast cartoon "This Is a White Man's Government" (Harper's Weekly, September 5, 1868) is real with the exact attributes described (three figures, Confederate + "5 Points" + "5th Avenue"); Reconstruction-era Black voter registration and officeholder numbers in SC/MS/LA are composited from Congressional records and Du Bois's *Black Reconstruction* appendices (specific numbers for S. Carolina 1867 registered Black voters ~80,550 is accurate within 1-2%); the Joint Select Committee on the condition of affairs in the late insurrectionary states (1871, the "Klan Committee" reports) is real and its testimony is in the public record; W.E.B. Du Bois's *Black Reconstruction in America* (1935) is real with the "slave went free; stood a brief moment in the sun" quote authentic; the College Board 7-point DBQ rubric structure (thesis, contextualization, evidence up to 3 pts, source analysis, complexity) is accurate as of the 2026 exam cycle; "Dunning School" as a 1905-era historiographical framework is the correct term; Eric Foner's argument that the Slaughter-House Cases (1873) gutted the "privileges or immunities" clause is a standard reading in modern Reconstruction scholarship. 0013 — Series A SaaS financial archetypes are plausible ($12M ARR, 28% YoY growth, 112% NRR, $1.1M/mo burn, 78% gross margin all sit within normal Series A ranges for B2B SaaS in 2026); pipeline coverage of 3.8x at start-of-quarter is a standard B2B SaaS rule of thumb; Rule of 40 (ARR growth + FCF margin ≥ 40) is the real Series B-ready threshold investors cite; "burn multiple" (net burn ÷ net new ARR) is a real David Sacks-popularized metric with 2.0x as a commonly cited healthy threshold; January-hired eng headcount at ~$50K/mo fully loaded is accurate for senior SF/remote engineers; 2-month severance for mid-tier layoffs is a common package; 19% customer concentration (top-3 accounts) is a real concentration risk threshold that investors ask about; Datadog / Salesforce / external counsel as the "top 3 vendor line items to renegotiate" is realistic for a Series A SaaS. No invented frameworks, no invented metrics, no invented macro narratives.

(b) 0013 step 5's framework section explicitly calls out "add expansion pipeline coverage at $25M+ ARR" — that's a transferable pattern to other category signal frameworks and could seed a future Strategy or Data project around "signal frameworks for non-finance teams." (c) The 9-slide deck-in-markdown pattern from iter 61's 0010 step 4 shows up again in 0012's rubric-as-artifact and 0013's memo-as-artifact — "the step IS the deliverable" is now a well-established pattern across ~5 projects, worth canonicalizing in a BACKLOG note for future content iters. (d) At 13/50 projects, the seed file is 3,729 lines — the whole file is still well under any sane editor limit, but around 25/50 the append-only pattern may start to slow iter reads; BACKLOG could flag "at 25 projects, consider splitting by-category into sub-files" as a structural question for Drew. (e) teacherben's Canvas LMS reference in 0012 and the "Dovetail" reference in iter 61's 0010 point at a pattern: real-world tool names make projects feel authentic, and `tools_used` array might eventually get a dedicated UI facet (filterable by tool). Worth flagging for a future Polish iter as a Browse-page enhancement.
